Qada for a Prisoner Who Estimated Ramadan
Explains the ruling on a prisoner who estimates Ramadan and the required qada when his estimation was wrong.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the required qada days when a prisoner's estimated fast does not match the actual Ramadan, applying the Hanafi rule that qada is based on the number of days missed.

Core Idea
A prisoner's estimated fast is valid only if it coincides with the actual Ramadan; otherwise, qada is based on days missed, not lunar months.

This lesson examines a detailed ruling from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq about a prisoner in dar al-harb who is uncertain about the beginning of Ramadan and fasts based on estimation (taharrin). The passage systematically explores outcomes depending on whether the estimated month matches Ramadan, Shawwal, Dhul-Hijjah, or another month, and how many days must be made up. The key principle: qada is by the number of days, not the lunar month.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Scenario and Coincidence with Ramadan
Identify the core situation: a prisoner in dar al-harb, uncertain about Ramadan, fasts by estimation. If the estimated month coincides exactly with actual Ramadan, the fast is valid. If it precedes, it is invalid.
This is the baseline: validity depends on exact match.
2
Analyze Coincidence with Shawwal
If the estimated month coincides with Shawwal (after Ramadan), validity requires matching month lengths and specified intention at night. Calculate qada: if both complete, make up 1 day (Eid). If Ramadan complete and Shawwal deficient, make up 2 days (Eid + deficiency). If opposite, nothing is owed.
Note that no separate qada intention is required.
3
Analyze Coincidence with Dhul-Hijjah
If the estimated month coincides with Dhul-Hijjah, qada includes prohibited days. If both months complete, qada = 4 days (Nahr + 3 Tashriq). If Ramadan complete and Dhul-Hijjah deficient, qada = 5 days. If opposite, qada = 3 days.
The days of Nahr and Tashriq are haram for fasting, so they must be made up.
4
Consider Other Months and Multiple Years
For any other month, no qada if both months equal or Ramadan deficient; if Ramadan complete and other deficient, qada = 1 day. For multiple years, if the intention was absolute (mubham), it covers past missing Ramadans; if specified to a particular year, it does not.
Authenticated in al-Muhit.
5
Apply the General Principle
Throughout, qada is based on the exact number of days missed, not the lunar month. The examples of the sick person and the vow confirm this: qada must equal the count of missed days.
This is a foundational Hanafi principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنه يتفرع على كيفية النية ووقتها مسألة الأسير في دار الحرب إذا اشتبه عليه رمضان فتحرى وصام شهراً عن رمضان فلا يخلو إما أن يوافق أو لا بالتقديم أو بالتأخير، فإن وافق جاز، وإن تقدم لم يجز، وإن تأخر فإن وافق شوّالاً يجوز بشرط موافقة الشهرين في العدد وتعيين النية وتبييتها ولا يشترط نية القضاء في الصحيح فإن كان كل منهما كاملاً قضى يوماً واحداً لأجل يوم الفطر، وإن كان رمضان كاملاً وشوّال ناقصاً قضى يومين يوماً لأجل يوم العيد ويوماً لأجل النقصان وعلى العكس لا شيء عليه. وإن وافق صومه هلال ذي الحجة، فإن كان رمضان كاملاً وذو الحجة كاملاً قضى أربعة أيام النحر وأيام التشريق، وإن كان رمضان كاملاً وذو الحجة ناقصاً قضى خمسة أيام وعلى عكسه قضى ثلاثة أيام، وإن وافق صومه شهراً آخر سوى هذين الشهرين، فإن كان الشهران كاملين أو ناقصين أو كان رمضان ناقصاً والآخر كاملاً فلا شيء عليه، وعلى عكسه قضى يوماً. ولو صام بالتحري سنين كثيرة ثم تبين أنه صام في كل سنة قبل شهر رمضان فهل يجوز صومه في الثانية عن الأولى وفي الثالثة عن الثانية وفي الرابعة عن الثالثة؟ قيل يجوز، وقيل لا يجوز. كذا في البدائع مختصراً. وصحح في المحيط أنه إن نوى صوم رمضان مبهماً يجوز عن القضاء، وإن نوى عن السنة الثانية مفسراً لا يجوز، وقد علم هذا أن من من فاته رمضان وكان ناقصاً يلزمه قضاؤه بعدد الأيام لاشهر كامل، ولهذا قال في البدائع : قالوا فيمن أفطر شهراً بعذر ثلاثين يوماً ثم قضى شهراً بالهلال فكان تسعة وعشرين أن عليه قضاء يوم آخر لأن المعتبر عدد الأيام التي أفطر فيها دون الهلال لأن القضاء على قدر الفائت، ولو صام أهل مصر تسعة وعشرين وأفطروا للرؤية وفيهم مريض لم يصم، فإن علم ما صام أهل مصره فعليه قضاء تسعة وعشرين يوماً، وإن لم يعلم صام ثلاثين يوماً لأنه الأصل والنقصان عارض ا هـ . وفي عدة الفتاوى: لو قال الله علي صوم شوّال وذي القعدة وذي الحجة فصامهن بالرؤية وكان هلال ذي القعدة وذي الحجة ثلاثين وشوال تسعة وعشرين فعليه صوم خمسة أيام الفطر والأضحية وأيام التشريق، ولو قال الله ثلاثة أشهر فصامهن فعليه قضاء تسعة أيام لأنه أشار إلى غائب فيلزم لكل شهر ثلاثون ا هـ. وبما ذكرنا علم من يراجع فتح القدير أنه لم يستوف الأقسام كلها.
And know that there branches from the manner and time of intention the issue of the prisoner in the land of war if Ramadan is ambiguous to him, so he estimates and fasts a month for Ramadan. Then it is either that it coincides [with the actual Ramadan] or not, either by being before or after. If it coincides, it is valid. If it is before, it is not valid. If it is after, then if it coincides with Shawwal, it is valid on condition that the two months match in number, and that the intention is specified and made at night, and specifying the intention for qada is not required in the correct view. If both are complete, he makes up one day because of the day of Fitr. If Ramadan is complete and Shawwal is deficient, he makes up two days: one for the day of Eid and one for the deficiency. And on the opposite [Ramadan deficient, Shawwal complete] nothing is upon him. If his fast coincides with the crescent of Dhul-Hijjah, then if Ramadan is complete and Dhul-Hijjah is complete, he makes up four days: the day of Nahr and the days of Tashriq. If Ramadan is complete and Dhul-Hijjah is deficient, he makes up five days. On the opposite [Ramadan deficient, Dhul-Hijjah complete], he makes up three days. If his fast coincides with another month besides these two, then if the two months are both complete or both deficient, or if Ramadan is deficient and the other is complete, nothing is upon him. On the opposite [Ramadan complete and other deficient], he makes up one day. If he fasts by estimation for many years, then it becomes clear that he fasted in every year before Ramadan, is his fast in the second year valid for the first, and in the third for the second, and in the fourth for the third? It was said: yes, and it was said: no. Thus in al-Bada'i' briefly. And it was authenticated in al-Muhit that if he intended the fast of Ramadan in an absolute sense, it is valid for qada, and if he intended it specifically for the second year, it is not valid. And it is known from this that to whom Ramadan was missed and it was deficient, he is obligated to make it up with the count of days of a complete month. Hence they said in al-Bada'i': regarding one who broke a month due to an excuse for thirty days, then made up a month by the [sighting of the] crescent, and it was twenty-nine, that he must make up another day because the consideration is the number of days he broke, not the crescent, because qada is according to what was missed. And if the people of a city fast twenty-nine and break due to sighting, and among them is a sick person who did not fast, then if he knows the count that his city fasted, he must make up twenty-nine days; if he does not know, he fasts thirty days because that is the original, and deficiency is incidental. And in 'Iddat al-Fatawa: if someone says: I am obligated to fast Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and Dhu al-Hijjah, and he fasts them by sighting, and the crescents of Dhu al-Qa'dah and Dhu al-Hijjah were thirty, and Shawwal twenty-nine, then he must fast five days: the day of Fitr, the day of Adha, and the days of Tashriq. If he says: I am obligated to fast three months, and he fasts them, then he must make up nine days because he pointed to an absent entity, so for each month thirty days are necessary. And by what we mentioned, whoever refers to Fath al-Qadir should know that he did not exhaust all the divisions.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a complex case about a prisoner in enemy territory (dar al-harb) who is uncertain about the start of Ramadan. He makes an estimation (taharrin) and fasts a month intending Ramadan. The text then systematically examines scenarios based on whether his estimated month coincides with the actual Ramadan, precedes it, or follows it. If it coincides exactly, the fast is valid. If it precedes, it is invalid. If it follows, and coincides with Shawwal, it is valid provided the month lengths match and intention was made at night; no separate intention for qada is required in the correct view. The number of make-up days depends on the match of month lengths and whether it coincided with Ramadan, Shawwal, or Dhul-Hijjah. For example, if Ramadan was 30 days and Shawwal 29, he must make up 2 days (one for Eid and one for the deficiency). If his fast coincided with Dhul-Hijjah, he must make up four or five days depending on completeness, to cover the days of Nahr and Tashriq when fasting is prohibited. If it coincided with another month, generally no make-up is required unless Ramadan was complete and the other deficient. The text also discusses the scenario where this happens over multiple years; the correct view is that if he intended the obligation in general (mubham), it counts for the past missed Ramadans, but if he intended a specific year, it does not. The passage concludes with a principle: qada is based on the number of days missed, not the lunar month's sighting, and provides examples from al-Bada'i' and 'Iddat al-Fatawa to illustrate.

Key Terms
تحري (taharrin): Estimation or striving to determine the correct Ramadan when uncertain, such as for a prisoner in dar al-harb.
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed obligatory fast. The number of days must equal the days missed, not based on lunar months.
أيام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The three days following the Day of Sacrifice (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul-Hijjah); fasting on these days is haram (prohibited) except for those performing tamattu' or qiran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A prisoner estimates Ramadan and fasts a month, which later turns out to coincide with Shawwal (post-Ramadan). Ramadan was 30 days and Shawwal was 30 days. How many days must he make up?
A) Nothing, because the month lengths match.
B) One day, because of the day of Fitr (Eid al-Fitr).
C) Two days, because of Eid and the matching deficiency.
D) 29 days, because qada is based on Shawwal's days.

Key Takeaway
Qada of missed fasts is wajib based on the exact number of days missed; the lunar month's crescent is irrelevant for qada.

Definition of Mustahabb, Mandub, and Nafl
Resolving terminological differences on mustahabb, mandub, and nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the definitions of mustahabb, mandub, and nafl according to Hanafi usul scholars and fuqaha, and state the preferred position.

Core Idea
Mustahabb and mandub are synonymous in Hanafi usul; nafl is the broad category of voluntary worship.

The terms mustahabb, mandub, and nafl are often used interchangeably, but classical Hanafi scholars debated subtle distinctions. This passage clarifies the definitions offered by usul scholars versus the fuqaha, resolving an internal terminological dispute and explaining the broader scope of nafl. Understanding these nuances is essential for correctly categorizing voluntary acts in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scholarly groups and their definitions
The passage contrasts the views of usul scholars (al-usuliyyun) and the fuqaha. Usul scholars hold that mustahabb and mandub are identical: any recommended act the Prophet consistently performed is sunnah, and what he did inconsistently is mandub/mustahabb. The fuqaha differentiate: mustahabb is an act done once and left another time, while mandub is done once or twice to teach permissibility.
This is an intra-Hanafi terminological difference, not a dispute over rulings.
2
Note the preferred view and its justification
The author favors the usul scholars' view, critiquing the author of al-Bahr for inconsistency and noting that al-Muhit defined mustahabb in a way that others used for mandub. The preference is based on clarity and avoiding confusion.
The tarjih is from the author himself and later scholars.
3
Understand the linguistic and Shar'i meaning of nafl
Linguistically, nafl means 'increase'. In Shari'ah, it refers to extra worship prescribed for us, not upon us, thus encompassing all voluntary acts (sunnah, mustahabb, mandub).
Nafl is the broadest category.
4
Recognize the narrow usage of nafl in the matn
In the passage, 'nafl' is sometimes used in contrast to masnun and mandub, meaning the lowest category of voluntary acts. This contextual usage should not be confused with the broader definition.
Be aware of context when reading fiqh texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال بعض الفضلاء: فما في البحر غير ظاهر فضلاً عن أن يكون أظهر، وما في الفتح من الاستدلال بالإجماع غير محرر قوله : (وينبغي أن يكون كل صوم الخ اعلم أن الذي عليه الأصوليون عدم الفرق بين المستحب والمندوب وأن ما واظب عليه مع ترك ما بلا عذر سنة ، وما لم يواظب عليه مندوب ومستحب، وإن لم يفعله بعد ما رغب فيه. كذا في التحرير. وعند الفقهاء : المستحب ما فعله النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم مرة وتركه أخرى، والمندوب ما فعله مرة أو مرتين تعليماً للجواز. كذا في شرح النقاية. قال المؤلف في كتاب الطهارة ويرد عليه ما رغب فيه ولم يفعله وما جعله تعريفاً للمستحب جعله في المحيط تعريفاً للمندوب فالأولى ما عليه الأصوليون | ثم النفل في اللغة الزيادة، وفي الشريعة زيادة عبادة شرعت لنا لا علينا فيشمل الأقسام الثلاثة، ولذا ترجم المصنف بقوله «باب الوتر والنوافل لكن المراد بالنفل في كلام الفتح ما قابل المسنون والمندوب وظاهره أن المراد به ما رادف
Some virtuous one said: What is in al-Bahr is not apparent, let alone being more apparent; and what is in al-Fath from deducing by consensus is not verified. His statement: 'And it should be that every fast...' Know that what the usul scholars hold is that there is no difference between mustahabb and mandub, and that what he consistently did while abandoning it without excuse is sunnah, and what he did not consistently do is mandub and mustahabb, even if he did not do it after encouraging it. Thus in al-Tahrir. And according to the fuqaha: mustahabb is what the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, did once and left at another time; and mandub is what he did once or twice to teach permissibility. Thus in Sharh al-Nuqaya. The author said in the Book of Purity: And it is objected to it that which he encouraged and did not do, and what he made as a definition for mustahabb, al-Muhit made as a definition for mandub. So the preferable is what the usul scholars hold. Then nafl in language is increase, and in the Shari'ah it is the increase of worship prescribed for us, not upon us, so it includes the three categories. That is why the author titled his section 'Chapter of Witr and Nawafil', but the intended meaning of nafl in the speech of al-Fath is what contrasts with masnun and mandub, and its apparent meaning is that it is synonymous with...
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hathiya-style) on the definitions of mustahabb, mandub, and nafl. It begins by critiquing the author's earlier comments, then clarifies the terminology. According to usul scholars, mustahabb and mandub are synonymous: any recommended act the Prophet consistently performed is sunnah, and what he did without consistency is mandub/mustahabb. The fuqaha differentiate: mustahabb is something the Prophet did once and left another time; mandub is something he did once or twice to demonstrate permissibility. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq himself previously defined mustahabb in a way that al-Muhit used for mandub, causing inconsistency. The preferred view is that of the usul scholars. Nafl linguistically means 'increase', and in Shari'ah it refers to extra worship prescribed for us, not upon us, thus encompassing all voluntary acts. In the matn, 'nafl' is used in contrast to masnun and mandub, meaning the lowest category of voluntary actions.

Key Terms
مُسْتَحَبّ (mustahabb): An act the Prophet did once and left another time (fuqaha) or any recommended act (usul scholars).
مَنْدُوب (mandub): An act the Prophet did once or twice to teach permissibility (fuqaha); synonymous with mustahabb (usul).
نَفْل (nafl): Extra worship; broadly includes all voluntary acts, but in some contexts contrasts with sunnah and mandub.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the preferred view on the relation between mustahabb and mandub?
A) Mustahabb is more emphasized than mandub
B) Mandub is a subset of mustahabb
C) There is no difference between them
D) Mustahabb is sunnah, mandub is nafl

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, mustahabb and mandub are synonymous; nafl is the overarching category for voluntary worship.

Establishing Ramadan: Sighting the Crescent or Completing Sha'ban
Ruling with proof from hadith and procedural furu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two valid methods for establishing Ramadan and cite the hadith proof that mandates them in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Ramadan begins only by actual sighting of the crescent or upon completing 30 days of Sha'ban – no other method is accepted.

The start of Ramadan is a matter of worship requiring certainty. The Hanafi school follows the explicit command of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as recorded in the authentic hadith. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its evidence, showing how the school balances textual proof with practical necessity when sighting is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling from the matn
The matn states: 'Ramadan is established by the sighting of its crescent or after thirty days of Sha'ban.' Recognise this as the core legal rule (hukm) for beginning the fast.
This is a wajib determination – fasting is contingent upon it.
2
Extract the primary proof (dalil)
The commentator cites the hadith from the two Sahihs: 'Fast at its sighting and break your fast at its sighting, and if it is obscured to you, then complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty days.' Locate this hadith as the sole textual basis.
The hadith is ahad, but its transmission (thubut) is qat'i (certain) via Bukhari and Muslim, and its indication (dalala) is qat'i as well.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof yields the ruling)
The imperative 'صوموا' (fast) indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul. The conditional clause 'فإن غم عليك' provides the alternative: if the moon is not seen, complete 30 days. This shows that sighting is the default and completion is the fallback – no other method (e.g., calculation) is permitted.
The Hanafi school holds that this imperative is 'amm and qat'i, binding on all instances.
4
Note the procedural application in court
The passage briefly describes a legal procedure: a claimant with an agency contingent on Ramadan's entry can prove the month via witnesses, with the opponent denying entry. This illustrates how the ruling is enforced judicially.
This is a practical furu' showing how the ruling interacts with qada (judicial process).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ويثبت رمضان برؤية هلاله أو بعد شعبان ثلاثين يوماً) لحديث الصحيحين «صوموا لرؤيته وأفطروا لرؤيته، فإن غم عليك فأكملوا عدة شعبان ثلاثين يوماً». والوجه في إثبات الرمضانية والعيد أن يدعي عند القاضي بوكالة رجل معلقة بدخول رمضان بقبض دين فيقر الخصم بالوكالة وينكر دخول رمضان فيشهد الشهود بذلك فيقضي الثالثة قوله: (وصحيح في المحيط الخ هذا التفصيل ذكره في البدائع أيضاً لكن بدون تصريح بالتصحيح فقال : وفصل الفقيه أبو جعفر في ذلك تفصيلاً فقال : إن صام في السنة الثانية عن الواجب عليه إلا أنه على ظن أنه في رمضان يجوز، وكذا في السنة الثالثة والرابعة لأنه صام عن الواجب عليه والواجب عليه قضاء رمضان الأول دون الثاني، وإن صام في السنة الثانية عن وفي الثالثة عن الرابعة لم يجز وعليه قضاء الرمضانات كلها ثم قال وضرب له أي أبو جعفر مثلاً وهو رجل اقتدى بالإمام على ظن أنه زيد فإذا هو عمر وصح اقتداؤه، ولو اقتدى بزيد فإذا هو عمر ولم يصح لأنه في الأول اقتدى بالإمام إلا أنه ظن أنه زيد فأخطأ. في ظنه وهذا لا يقدح في صحة الاقتداء بالإمام، وفي الثاني اقتدى بزيد فإذا لم يكن زيداً تبين أنه لم يقتد بأحد كذلك هنا إذا نوى صوم كل سنة عن الواجب عليه تعلقت نية الواجب بما عليه لا بالأول والثاني إلا أنه ظن أنه للثاني فأخطأ في ظنه فيقع عن الواجب عليه لا عما ظن ا هـ قوله : فيقر الخصم بالوكالة) قال الرملي : عبارة النهر فيقر بالدين والوكالة وينكر الدخول وكلاهما مشكل إذ لا ينفذ الإقرار على الغائب
His statement: (And Ramadan is established by the sighting of its crescent or after thirty days of Sha'ban) due to the hadith of the two Sahihs: 'Fast at its sighting and break your fast at its sighting, and if it is obscured to you, then complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty days.' And the manner of establishing [the beginning of] Ramadan and Eid is that one claims before the judge by an agency of a man contingent upon the entry of Ramadan for taking a debt, so the opponent acknowledges the agency and denies the entry of Ramadan, so the witnesses testify to that, and he judges the third. His statement: (And it is authenticated in al-Muhit, etc. This detail was mentioned in al-Bada'i' as well but without explicit authentication. He said: And al-Faqih Abu Ja'far detailed it and said: If he fasts in the second year for the obligation upon him, but he opines that it is Ramadan, it is valid; likewise in the third and fourth years because he fasted for the obligation upon him, and the obligation upon him is the qada of the first Ramadan, not the second. If he fasts in the second year for the third and in the third for the fourth, it is not valid and he must make up all the Ramadans. Then he gave an example: a man who prays behind an imam opining that he is Zayd, but he is actually 'Umar – his prayer is valid. If he intended to follow Zayd and it turned out to be 'Umar, it is not valid because in the first he followed the imam but thought it was Zayd, and this error does not harm the validity of following the imam; in the second, he followed Zayd, and when it was not Zayd, it became clear that he followed no one. Similarly here, if he intends the fast of every year for the obligation upon him, his intention attaches to what is upon him, not to the first or second, except that he thinks it is for the second, so his opinion is wrong; it falls for the obligation upon him, not for what he thought. End quote. His statement: (So the opponent acknowledges the agency) al-Ramli said: The expression of al-Nahr: he acknowledges the debt and the agency and denies the entry [of Ramadan], and both are problematic because acknowledgment cannot take effect on behalf of an absent person.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq begins with the core ruling on establishing Ramadan. The matn (of Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states that Ramadan is proven either by actually sighting the crescent moon or by completing 30 days of Sha'ban if the moon is not seen. The commentator cites the well-known hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim: 'Fast when you see it, break your fast when you see it, and if it is obscured, then complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty days.' This hadith is the primary textual evidence (dalil naqli) for the ruling. The text then shifts to a discussion of how to legally prove the start of Ramadan in a court: through witness testimony and a procedure involving a claim of agency. However, the commentary quickly digresses into a long citation from al-Muhit and al-Bada'i' returning to the earlier issue of the prisoner's fast over multiple years, providing an analogy from prayer (following an imam). This analogy clarifies that if a person fasts for the obligation upon him (qada of first missed Ramadan) but mistakenly thinks he is fasting for the current Ramadan, it is valid because his intention attached to the actual obligation, not the mistaken label. The passage ends with a critique of al-Ramli regarding the court procedure for acknowledging agency. The key point for the student is the primary ruling: Ramadan is established by sighting or completing 30 days, and the hadith is the proof.

Key Terms
رؤية الهلال (ru'yat al-hilal): The sighting of the new crescent moon that marks the beginning of a lunar month, specifically Ramadan.
إكمال عدة شعبان (ikmal 'iddat Sha'ban): Completing the month of Sha'ban to 30 days when the crescent for Ramadan cannot be sighted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the passage, what should Muslims do if the crescent for Ramadan is not visible due to clouds?
A) Use astronomical calculations to determine the start of Ramadan.
B) Assume the moon would be visible and begin fasting immediately.
C) Complete the month of Sha'ban to 30 days, then begin Ramadan.
D) Wait for confirmation from another country and then start fasting.

Key Takeaway
Ramadan is only established by actual sighting of the crescent or by completing 30 days of Sha'ban, based on the direct command of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

The Prisoner's Fast: Intention for Qada and Analogy in Fiqh
Ruling with analogy on intention in fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the analogy of following an imam to determine the validity of a prisoner's fast when he intends the obligation upon him but mistakes its specific year.

Core Idea
A prisoner's fast counts for qada if he intends the obligation upon him, even if he mistakenly thinks it is for the current Ramadan.

This lesson clarifies a practical scenario: a prisoner who misses multiple Ramadans and then fasts, intending each fast for the obligation due on him. The Hanafi jurists use a powerful analogy from prayer (following an imam) to show that the intention's object is the actual obligation, not the mistaken label. Understanding this analogy deepens your grasp of how intention and error interact in worship.

Guided Path
1
Understand the prisoner's scenario
al-Faqih Abu Ja'far presents a case: a prisoner fasts in the second year intending the qada of the first Ramadan, but mistakenly thinks he is fasting for the current Ramadan (the second). The ruling: his fast is valid if he intended 'the obligation upon him' (الواجب عليه). If he explicitly intended the second Ramadan but actually owes the first, the fast is invalid.
The key distinction is whether his intention attaches to the abstract obligation or to a specific mistaken time.
2
Analyse the analogy (tashbih) with prayer
The analogy: a man prays behind an imam thinking the imam is Zayd, but it turns out to be 'Umar. His prayer is valid because in reality he followed the imam, not Zayd. If he intended to follow Zayd and it turned out to be 'Umar, his prayer is invalid because he followed no actual imam.
The common illa (effective cause) is that the intention attaches to the real entity (imam/obligation), not the mistaken belief.
3
Apply the analogy to the fast
Similarly, if the prisoner intends 'the fast that is wajib upon me' (the qada obligation), his intention attaches to the actual qada due, even if he mistakenly assumes it is for the current Ramadan. The fast fulfills the qada. But if he intends 'the fast of the second Ramadan' without reference to the obligation, and that is not Ramadan, his intention is misplaced and the fast is invalid.
This shows the Hanafi principle that intention (niyyah) is effective when directed at the essential legal obligation, not at a specific time that may be mistaken.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Making Up Missed Ramadans: Vague vs Specific Intention
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada intention with analogy to prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi ruling on making up multiple missed Ramadans and APPLY the distinction between vague and specific intention to determine the validity of qada.

Core Idea
A vague intention for missed Ramadan counts; a specific intention for the wrong year invalidates the fast.

The fiqh of making up missed fasts is straightforward when only one Ramadan was missed. But when multiple years are missed, the issue becomes: to which year does each qada fast apply? This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute and its resolution, using an analogy from prayer intention to clarify the role of intention in qada.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on qada
The obligation of qada for missed Ramadan is wajib. The issue here is the validity of the qada fast when multiple Ramadans are missed.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Early opinions differed: some said making up with specific intention for later years is valid, others said it is not. Abu Ja'far provided a detailed distinction.
3
Understand the corrected view (tarjih)
Al-Muhit and Bada'i' endorse Abu Ja'far's distinction: vague intention (mubham) counts; specific intention for a later year (mufassar) does not.
4
Trace the qiyas analogy
The ruling is analogized to following an imam in prayer: general intention to follow is valid even if mistaken identity; specific intention to follow a particular person invalidates if mistaken.
The illa is that intention attaches to the obligation generally, not to a specific person or year.
5
Apply to multiple missed Ramadans
If one intends generally for 'the missed Ramadan', it counts for the earliest due. If one intends specifically for a later year, the fast does not count for any missed obligation.

رمضان فهل يجوز صومه في الثانية عن الأولى وفي الثالثة عن الثانية وفي الرابعة عن الثالثة؟ قيل يجوز، وقيل لا يجوز. كذا في البدائع مختصراً. وصحح في المحيط أنه إن نوى صوم رمضان مبهماً يجوز عن القضاء، وإن نوى عن السنة الثانية مفسراً لا يجوز، وقد علم هذا أن من من فاته رمضان وكان ناقصاً يلزمه قضاؤه بعدد الأيام لاشهر كامل، ولهذا قال في البدائع : قالوا فيمن أفطر شهراً بعذر ثلاثين يوماً ثم قضى شهراً بالهلال فكان تسعة وعشرين أن عليه قضاء يوم آخر لأن المعتبر عدد الأيام التي أفطر فيها دون الهلال لأن القضاء على قدر الفائت، ولو صام أهل مصر تسعة وعشرين وأفطروا للرؤية وفيهم مريض لم يصم، فإن علم ما صام أهل مصره فعليه قضاء تسعة وعشرين يوماً، وإن لم يعلم صام ثلاثين يوماً لأنه الأصل والنقصان عارض ا هـ . وفي عدة الفتاوى: لو قال الله علي صوم شوّال وذي القعدة وذي الحجة فصامهن بالرؤية وكان هلال ذي القعدة وذي الحجة ثلاثين ونوال تسعة وعشرين فعليه صوم خمسة أيام الفطر والأضحية وأيام التشريق، ولو قال الله ثلاثة أشهر فصامهن فعليه قضاء تسعة أيام لأنه أشار إلى غائب فيلزم لكل شهر علي صوم ثلاثون ا هـ. وبما ذكرنا علم من يراجع فتح القدير أنه لم يستوف الأقسام كلها. قوله: (وصحيح في المحيط الخ هذا التفصيل ذكره في البدائع أيضاً لكن بدون تصريح بالتصحيح فقال : وفصل الفقيه أبو جعفر في ذلك تفصيلاً فقال : إن صام في السنة الثانية عن الواجب عليه إلا أنه على ظن أنه في رمضان يجوز، وكذا في السنة الثالثة والرابعة لأنه صام عن الواجب عليه والواجب عليه قضاء رمضان الأول دون الثاني، وإن صام في السنة الثانية عن وفي الثالثة عن الرابعة لم يجز وعليه قضاء الرمضانات كلها ثم قال وضرب له أي أبو جعفر مثلاً وهو رجل اقتدى بالإمام على ظن أنه زيد فإذا هو عمر وصح اقتداؤه، ولو اقتدى بزيد فإذا هو عمر ولم يصح لأنه في الأول اقتدى بالإمام إلا أنه ظن أنه زيد فأخطأ. في ظنه وهذا لا يقدح في صحة الاقتداء بالإمام، وفي الثاني اقتدى بزيد فإذا لم يكن زيداً تبين أنه لم يقتد بأحد كذلك هنا إذا نوى صوم كل سنة عن الواجب عليه تعلقت نية الواجب بما عليه لا بالأول والثاني إلا أنه ظن أنه للثاني فأخطأ في ظنه فيقع عن الواجب عليه لا عما ظن ا هـ
Ramadan: Is it permissible to fast in the second year for the first, in the third for the second, and in the fourth for the third? It was said permissible and said not permissible. Briefly in Bada'i'. And it was corrected in Al-Muhit that if he intended the Ramadan fast vaguely, it is valid for the qada, and if he intended specifically for the second year, it is not valid. And it is known from this that whoever missed Ramadan and it was deficient, he must make it up with the number of days of the complete month. For this, Bada'i' said: They said concerning one who broke fast for a month due to an excuse of thirty days, then made up a month by the crescent and it was twenty-nine days, that he must make up another day because consideration is the number of days he broke, not the crescent, because qada is based on the missed amount. And if the people of a city fasted twenty-nine and broke for sighting, and among them there is a sick person who did not fast, then if he knows what the people of his city fasted, he must make up twenty-nine days, and if he does not know, he fasts thirty because that is the original and deficiency is an exception. In 'Iddat al-Fatawa: If someone says 'upon me is fasting Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, and Dhul Hijjah', and he fasts them by sighting, and it turns out that Dhul Qa'dah and Dhul Hijjah were thirty and Shawwal twenty-nine, then he must fast five days: the day of Fitr, the day of Adha, and the days of Tashreeq. And if he says 'upon me is three months' and fasts them, then he must make up nine days because he indicated absent months, so each month requires thirty days. By what we have mentioned, it is known that whoever reviews Fath al-Qadir did not cover all categories. He said: (And it is corrected in Al-Muhit etc. This detail was mentioned in Bada'i' as well but without explicit correction. He said: Abu Ja'far gave a detailed distinction: If he fasts in the second year for the obligation due on him, while thinking it is Ramadan, it is valid, likewise in the third and fourth, because he fasts for the obligation due on him, and the obligation on him is to make up the first missed Ramadan, not the second. And if he fasts in the second year specifically for the second, and in the third for the third, and in the fourth for the fourth, it is not valid, and he must make up all the missed Ramadans. Then he gave an example: a man follows the imam thinking he is Zaid, and it turns out to be Umar, and his following is valid; but if he intended specifically to follow Zaid and it turned out to be Umar, it is not valid. Because in the first, he intended to follow the imam but thought he was Zaid, and his mistake does not harm the validity of following the imam. In the second, he intended to follow Zaid and it turned out not to be Zaid, so it becomes clear he did not follow anyone. Similarly here, when he intends to fast each year for the obligation due on him, his intention attaches to what is due, not to the first or second, but he thought it was for the second, so his intention was wrong, and the fast counts for the obligation due, not for what he thought.) End.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the ruling for making up multiple missed Ramadans. The author begins by stating the question: if someone has missed several Ramadans, does fasting in subsequent years count for the earlier missed ones? There are two opinions. The correction from Al-Muhit is cited: if one intends the fast vaguely for 'the missed Ramadan' it counts; if one specifically intends it for a particular later year, it does not. Examples from Bada'i' and 'Iddat al-Fatawa are given to illustrate the principle that qada must be based on the number of days missed, not on lunar months. Then the commentary from Abu Ja'far is quoted, providing a thorough distinction between intending the obligation generally versus intending a specific year. The analogy of following the imam is used: if one intends to follow the imam generally (even if he mistakes his identity), it is valid; but if one intends specifically to follow a particular person and that person is not there, the prayer is invalid. Similarly, if one intends the obligatory fast generally, it counts for what is due, even if he mistakenly thought it was for a particular year. This is the relied-upon position according to Al-Muhit.

Key Terms
صوم رمضان (sawm ramadan): The obligatory fast of the month of Ramadan.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory fast after its time.
مبهم (mubham): Vague intention, i.e., intending the obligatory fast without specifying which missed Ramadan.
مفسر (mufassar): Specific intention, i.e., intending the fast for a particular missed Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the corrected view in Al-Muhit, if someone has missed three Ramadans and fasts in the fourth year with the specific intention of making up the third missed Ramadan, what is the ruling?
A) The fast counts for the third missed Ramadan.
B) The fast counts for the first missed Ramadan.
C) The fast does not count for any missed Ramadan.
D) The fast counts for the missed Ramadan due generally.

Key Takeaway
When making up multiple missed Ramadans, a vague intention suffices, but a specific intention for the wrong year renders the fast invalid as qada.

Sawm — Fasting

The Establishment of Ramadan: Ruling and Proof from Hadith
Ruling with hadith and commentary on the commencement of Ramadan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two methods of establishing Ramadan and explain why fasting does not depend on a court ruling.

Core Idea
Ramadan begins by sighting the crescent or completing 30 days of Sha'ban; court proof is not required for fasting.

Understanding how Ramadan begins is essential for every Muslim. The Prophet ﷺ gave clear guidance: fast when you see the moon, and if it is hidden, complete thirty days. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the primary evidence, and a key distinction: while a court declaration is needed for Eid, fasting Ramadan begins with personal knowledge or reliable news.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and basic ruling
The act is the commencement of fasting Ramadan. The ruling: it becomes obligatory by one of two methods – either sighting the crescent of Ramadan or completing 30 days of Sha'ban.
The ruling is fard 'ayn once established.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The author cites the well-known hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim: 'Fast for its sighting and break for its sighting, and if it is obscured, complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty days.'
This hadith is mutawatir in meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the evidence proves the ruling)
The imperative 'صوموا' (fast) indicates obligation. The conditional phrase 'فإن غم عليكم' (if it is obscured for you) establishes the alternative of completing thirty days. Thus, the ruling is derived directly from the text.
In Hanafi usul, the amr (command) indicates wujub.
4
Understand the distinction between Ramadan and Eid regarding court testimony
For Ramadan, mere sighting or completion of thirty days obligates fasting; no court ruling is needed. For Eid, testimony before a qadi is required because breaking the fast is a right of people (haqq al-'ibad) that may involve disputed payments or other claims.
This distinction is based on the nature of the obligation: individual worship vs. communal ruling.
5
Recognize that fasting does not depend on formal judicial proof
The commentator clarifies that the term 'thubut' in the matn means obligation or confirmation, not a court judgment. The cause for fasting is either sighting or completion, independent of the qadi's decision.
This resolves a potential confusion about needing a court declaration before fasting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ويثبت رمضان برؤية هلاله أو بعد شعبان ثلاثين يوماً) لحديث الصحيحين «صوموا لرؤيته وأفطروا لرؤيته، فإن غم عليك فأكملوا عدة شعبان ثلاثين يوماً»(۱). والوجه في إثبات الرمضانية والعيد أن يدعي عند القاضي بوكالة رجل معلقة بدخول رمضان بقبض دين فيقر الخصم بالوكالة وينكر دخول رمضان فيشهد الشهود بذلك فيقضي ثلاثين يوماً ولا يصام يوم الشك إلا تطوعاً ومن رأى هلال رمضان أو الفطر ورد قوله القاضي عليه بالمال فيثبت مجيء رمضان لأن إثبات مجيء رمضان لا يدخل تحت الحكم حتى لو أخبر رجل عدل القاضي بمجيء رمضان يقبل ويأمر الناس بالصوم يعني في يوم الغيم، ولا يشترط لفظ الشهادة وشرائط القضاء، أما في العيد فيشترط لفظ الشهاده وهو يدخل تحت الحكم لأنه من حقوق العباد كذا في الخلاصة من كتاب الشهادات. وبهذا علم أن عبارة المصنف في الوافي أولى وأوجز وهي: ويصام برؤية الهلال أو إكمال شعبان لأن الصوم لا يتوقف على الثبوت وليس يلزم من رؤيته ثبوته لما تقدم أن مجرد مجيئه لا يدخل تحت الحكم ولم يتعرض لوجوب التماسه ولا شك في وجوبه على الناس وجوب كفاية . وينبغي في كلام بعضهم بمعناه ووقته ليلة الثلاثين ولهذا قال في الاختيار : يجب التماسه في اليوم التاسع والعشرين وقت الغروب، وقول بعضهم في التاسع والعشرين تساهل. نعم لو رؤي في التاسع والعشرين بعد الزوال كان كرؤيته ليلة الثلاثين اتفاقاً، وإنما الخلاف في رؤيته قبل الزوال يوم الثلاثين؛ فعند أبي حنيفة ومحمد هو للمستقبلة، وعند أبي يوسف هو للماضية والمختار قولهما لكن لو أفطر إلا كفارة عليهم لأنهم أفطروا بتأويل . ذكره قاضيخان وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية وتكره الإشارة عند رؤية الهلال تحرزاً عن التشبه بأهل الجاهلية. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لا عبرة بقول المنجمين قال في غاية البيان: ومن يرجع فيه إلى قولهم فقد خالف الشرع لأنه روي عنه الله أنه قال «من أتى كاهناً أو قال : (لأن الصوم لا يتوقف على الثبوت الخ) قال في النهر : ليس في كلامه ما يفيد توقف الصوم على ثبوته يعني عند القاضي كما اقتضاه كلامه بل إن السبب لثبوته أحد هذين لا غير ا هـ . والظاهر أن المراد بالثبوت اللزوم والوجوب أي ويلزم صوم رمضان برؤية هلاله الخ. أو المراد التبين كما قاله الرملي
He said: (And Ramadan is established by sighting its crescent or after completing thirty days of Sha'ban) due to the hadith in the two Sahihs: 'Fast for its sighting and break for its sighting, and if it is obscured for you, then complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty days.' And the method for establishing the month of Ramadan and Eid is that a claim is made before the judge concerning an agency of a man suspended upon the entry of Ramadan for collecting a debt, so the opponent acknowledges the agency but denies the entry of Ramadan, and witnesses testify to that, and he judges for thirty days, and the day of doubt is not fasted except voluntarily. And whoever sees the crescent of Ramadan or Fitr and the judge reject his word, the judge rules against him in money, so the coming of Ramadan is established because establishing the coming of Ramadan does not fall under judgment; even if a just man informs the judge of the coming of Ramadan, he accepts and orders the people to fast, meaning on cloudy days, and the wording of testimony and the conditions of court are not required. As for Eid, the wording of testimony is required, and it falls under judgment because it pertains to the rights of people. This is in Al-Khulasa from the book of testimonies. By this it is known that the expression of the author in Al-Wafi is more appropriate and concise: 'Fasting is by sighting the crescent or completing the month of Sha'ban because fasting does not depend on formal proof, and its sighting does not necessitate proof for what has been stated that its mere coming does not fall under judgment, and he did not address the obligation of seeking it, and there is no doubt about its obligation on the people as a collective obligation.' And he said in some of his words to mean its time is the night of the thirtieth, and for this he said in Al-Ikhtiyar: 'Seeking it is obligatory on the twenty-ninth day at sunset,' and some people's saying on the twenty-ninth is lenient. Yes, if it is sighted on the twenty-ninth after noon, it is like sighting on the night of the thirtieth by agreement. The dispute is only about sighting it before noon on the thirtieth day; according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it is for the coming night; according to Abu Yusuf, it is for the past night, and the chosen view is theirs, but if they break the fast, there is expiation upon them because they broke with interpretation. Qadi Khan mentioned this, and in Al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah, pointing at the sighting of the crescent is disliked to avoid imitating the people of ignorance. The author indicated that there is no consideration of astrologers' statements. He said in Ghayat al-Bayan: Whoever relies on their statements has opposed the Shari'ah because it is narrated from him (peace be upon him) that he said: 'Whoever goes to a soothsayer...' Or he said: (Because fasting does not depend on proof) He said in Al-Nahr: There is nothing in his words that indicates fasting depends on proof, meaning before the judge as his words suggect, but rather the cause for its establishment is one of these two, nothing else. And it appears that the meaning of 'proof' is obligation and necessity, i.e., the obligation to fast Ramadan is established by sighting its crescent etc. Or it means confirmation as Al-Ramli said.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling and evidence for how Ramadan begins. The author quotes the famous hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim: 'Fast when you see the moon and break when you see it; if it is hidden, complete thirty days of Sha'ban.' The commentary discusses the difference between establishing Ramadan and establishing Eid in court: for Ramadan, the mere sighting obligates fasting without a court ruling; for Eid, testimony is required because it impacts the rights of people regarding breaking the fast. The author then addresses seeking the crescent on the night of the thirtieth, the ruling on sighting before noon, and the disapproval of relying on astrologers. He also clarifies that fasting does not depend on a court's proof; rather, the ruling is based on either sighting or completing thirty days. Finally, he notes the correction of a previous commentator's phrasing regarding the term 'thubut' (proof/establishment).

Key Terms
رؤية الهلال (ru'yat al-hilal): Sighting the new crescent moon that marks the beginning of a lunar month.
شعبان (sha'ban): The eighth lunar month, preceding Ramadan.
ثبوت (thubut): Establishment or proof, here meaning the commencement of Ramadan's obligation.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony, especially in court; for Ramadan, testimony is not required for fasting, but for Eid it is.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on fasting the day of shakk (doubt) if the sky is cloudy and the crescent was not sighted?
A) It is obligatory to fast.
B) It is recommended to fast.
C) It is allowed only as nafl (voluntary).
D) It is forbidden to fast.

Key Takeaway
Ramadan is established by sighting the crescent or completing 30 days of Sha'ban; fasting begins with certainty, not court approval.

Details of Crescent Sighting: Seeking, Sightings Before Noon, and Rejecting Astrology
Commentary on seeking the crescent, intra-Hanafi dispute, and related rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the obligation to seek the crescent on the 29th, the Hanafi ruling on sighting before noon, and the prohibition of relying on astrologers.

Core Idea
Seeking the crescent is wajib kifayah; sighting before noon on the 30th is for the coming night; astrologers' statements are disregarded.

Beyond the basic ruling, the Hanafi school details practical steps. It is obligatory (wajib kifayah) to seek the crescent on the evening of the 29th. If it is seen before noon on the 30th, a key dispute exists: does it count for the past night or the coming one? The school also prohibits relying on astrologers and discourages pointing at the moon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation to seek the crescent
The commentator affirms that seeking the crescent is wajib (obligatory) on the night of the 30th? Actually, it is obligatory on the 29th at sunset. The text says: 'يجب التماسه في اليوم التاسع والعشرين وقت الغروب' (seeking it is obligatory on the 29th day at the time of sunset).
This is a collective obligation (wajib kifayah).
2
Understand the time of seeking
The correct time is at sunset on the 29th. Some say 'on the 29th' which is lenient; the author clarifies it is specifically at sunset.
If sighted after noon on the 29th, it is considered as sighting on the night of the 30th by agreement.
3
Analyze the dispute on sighting before noon on the 30th
The key dispute: if the crescent is sighted before noon (zawal) on the 30th day of Sha'ban, does it indicate that the previous night was the start of Ramadan (i.e., the day is the 1st of Ramadan), or does it indicate the coming night? Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say it is for the coming night; Abu Yusuf says it is for the past night.
The chosen view (al-mukhtar) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
4
Examine the practical consequence (thamarah)
If a person mistakenly believes it is Eid and breaks the fast, then it turns out that day was still Ramadan, they must perform qada (make up) and kaffarah (expiation) if they deliberately broke the fast with an excuse of misinterpretation? Actually, the text says 'لكن لو أفطر إلا كفارة عليهم لأنهم أفطروا بتأويل' - they are not liable for kaffarah because they broke with a valid interpretation (ta'wil).
This is based on the chosen view.
5
Note the disapproval of pointing at the moon and rejecting astrology
Pointing at the crescent when sighting it is discouraged (makruh) to avoid imitating pre-Islamic practices. Also, relying on astrologers is against the Shari'a; the Prophet ﷺ said whoever goes to a soothsayer has rejected revelation.
The commentary from Ghayat al-Bayan emphasizes that astrology has no place in determining the lunar months.

قوله: (ويثبت رمضان برؤية هلاله أو بعد شعبان ثلاثين يوماً) لحديث الصحيحين «صوموا لرؤيته وأفطروا لرؤيته، فإن غم عليك فأكملوا عدة شعبان ثلاثين يوماً»(۱). والوجه في إثبات الرمضانية والعيد أن يدعي عند القاضي بوكالة رجل معلقة بدخول رمضان بقبض دين فيقر الخصم بالوكالة وينكر دخول رمضان فيشهد الشهود بذلك فيقضي ثلاثين يوماً ولا يصام يوم الشك إلا تطوعاً ومن رأى هلال رمضان أو الفطر ورد قوله القاضي عليه بالمال فيثبت مجيء رمضان لأن إثبات مجيء رمضان لا يدخل تحت الحكم حتى لو أخبر رجل عدل القاضي بمجيء رمضان يقبل ويأمر الناس بالصوم يعني في يوم الغيم، ولا يشترط لفظ الشهادة وشرائط القضاء، أما في العيد فيشترط لفظ الشهاده وهو يدخل تحت الحكم لأنه من حقوق العباد كذا في الخلاصة من كتاب الشهادات. وبهذا علم أن عبارة المصنف في الوافي أولى وأوجز وهي: ويصام برؤية الهلال أو إكمال شعبان لأن الصوم لا يتوقف على الثبوت وليس يلزم من رؤيته ثبوته لما تقدم أن مجرد مجيئه لا يدخل تحت الحكم ولم يتعرض لوجوب التماسه ولا شك في وجوبه على الناس وجوب كفاية . وينبغي في كلام بعضهم بمعناه ووقته ليلة الثلاثين ولهذا قال في الاختيار : يجب التماسه في اليوم التاسع والعشرين وقت الغروب، وقول بعضهم في التاسع والعشرين تساهل. نعم لو رؤي في التاسع والعشرين بعد الزوال كان كرؤيته ليلة الثلاثين اتفاقاً، وإنما الخلاف في رؤيته قبل الزوال يوم الثلاثين؛ فعند أبي حنيفة ومحمد هو للمستقبلة، وعند أبي يوسف هو للماضية والمختار قولهما لكن لو أفطر إلا كفارة عليهم لأنهم أفطروا بتأويل . ذكره قاضيخان وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية وتكره الإشارة عند رؤية الهلال تحرزاً عن التشبه بأهل الجاهلية. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لا عبرة بقول المنجمين قال في غاية البيان: ومن يرجع فيه إلى قولهم فقد خالف الشرع لأنه روي عنه الله أنه قال «من أتى كاهناً أو قال : (لأن الصوم لا يتوقف على الثبوت الخ) قال في النهر : ليس في كلامه ما يفيد توقف الصوم على ثبوته يعني عند القاضي كما اقتضاه كلامه بل إن السبب لثبوته أحد هذين لا غير ا هـ . والظاهر أن المراد بالثبوت اللزوم والوجوب أي ويلزم صوم رمضان برؤية هلاله الخ. أو المراد التبين كما قاله الرملي
He said: (And Ramadan is established by sighting its crescent or after completing thirty days of Sha'ban) due to the hadith in the two Sahihs: 'Fast for its sighting and break for its sighting, and if it is obscured for you, then complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty days.' And the method for establishing the month of Ramadan and Eid is that a claim is made before the judge concerning an agency of a man suspended upon the entry of Ramadan for collecting a debt, so the opponent acknowledges the agency but denies the entry of Ramadan, and witnesses testify to that, and he judges for thirty days, and the day of doubt is not fasted except voluntarily. And whoever sees the crescent of Ramadan or Fitr and the judge reject his word, the judge rules against him in money, so the coming of Ramadan is established because establishing the coming of Ramadan does not fall under judgment; even if a just man informs the judge of the coming of Ramadan, he accepts and orders the people to fast, meaning on cloudy days, and the wording of testimony and the conditions of court are not required. As for Eid, the wording of testimony is required, and it falls under judgment because it pertains to the rights of people. This is in Al-Khulasa from the book of testimonies. By this it is known that the expression of the author in Al-Wafi is more appropriate and concise: 'Fasting is by sighting the crescent or completing the month of Sha'ban because fasting does not depend on formal proof, and its sighting does not necessitate proof for what has been stated that its mere coming does not fall under judgment, and he did not address the obligation of seeking it, and there is no doubt about its obligation on the people as a collective obligation.' And he said in some of his words to mean its time is the night of the thirtieth, and for this he said in Al-Ikhtiyar: 'Seeking it is obligatory on the twenty-ninth day at sunset,' and some people's saying on the twenty-ninth is lenient. Yes, if it is sighted on the twenty-ninth after noon, it is like sighting on the night of the thirtieth by agreement. The dispute is only about sighting it before noon on the thirtieth day; according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it is for the coming night; according to Abu Yusuf, it is for the past night, and the chosen view is theirs, but if they break the fast, there is expiation upon them because they broke with interpretation. Qadi Khan mentioned this, and in Al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah, pointing at the sighting of the crescent is disliked to avoid imitating the people of ignorance. The author indicated that there is no consideration of astrologers' statements. He said in Ghayat al-Bayan: Whoever relies on their statements has opposed the Shari'ah because it is narrated from him (peace be upon him) that he said: 'Whoever goes to a soothsayer...' Or he said: (Because fasting does not depend on proof) He said in Al-Nahr: There is nothing in his words that indicates fasting depends on proof, meaning before the judge as his words suggect, but rather the cause for its establishment is one of these two, nothing else. And it appears that the meaning of 'proof' is obligation and necessity, i.e., the obligation to fast Ramadan is established by sighting its crescent etc. Or it means confirmation as Al-Ramli said.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling and evidence for how Ramadan begins. The author quotes the famous hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim: 'Fast when you see the moon and break when you see it; if it is hidden, complete thirty days of Sha'ban.' The commentary discusses the difference between establishing Ramadan and establishing Eid in court: for Ramadan, the mere sighting obligates fasting without a court ruling; for Eid, testimony is required because it impacts the rights of people regarding breaking the fast. The author then addresses seeking the crescent on the night of the thirtieth, the ruling on sighting before noon, and the disapproval of relying on astrologers. He also clarifies that fasting does not depend on a court's proof; rather, the ruling is based on either sighting or completing thirty days. Finally, he notes the correction of a previous commentator's phrasing regarding the term 'thubut' (proof/establishment).

Key Terms
التماس الهلال (talaab al-hilal): Seeking/sighting the crescent moon, especially on the 29th of Sha'ban.
قبل الزوال (qabl al-zawal): Before noon, the time of the dispute.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for breaking a fast; here not required due to ta'wil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, if the crescent of Ramadan is sighted before noon on the 30th of Sha'ban, what is the ruling?
A) That day is the 1st of Ramadan.
B) That day is still the 30th of Sha'ban, and Ramadan begins at sunset.
C) The day is considered the 1st of Ramadan only if the sighting is after noon.
D) The ruling depends on whether the sighting was by one or two people.

Key Takeaway
Seeking the crescent is a collective duty; the preferred view treats a pre-noon sighting on the 30th as indicating the next night's start, and astrologers are not to be followed.

Fasting the Day of Doubt: Intentions, Talawwum, and Taraddad
Expounds Hanafi rulings on fasting the day of doubt with various intentions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each type of intention on the day of doubt and apply the rules on hesitation in intention.

Core Idea
Intent on Ramadan on the day of doubt? It's makruh tahrimi—unless it's a habit; hesitation in essence voids the intention.

The day of doubt—the 30th of Sha‘ban—creates a unique tension between caution and prohibition. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position on fasting that day, examining the intentions, the recommended practice of talawwum, and the delicate rules of hesitation (taraddad) in intention. The passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq clarifies the rulings for judges, muftis, and the general public.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being judged (fasting on yawm al-shakk) and the hukm level for each possible intention. The passage distinguishes between intending Ramadan, another obligatory fast, a supererogatory fast, and hesitation.
The core ruling is that intending Ramadan with certainty is makruh tahriman, with an exception for habitual fasts.
2
Locate the dalīl and its application
The author cites the hadith prohibiting advancing Ramadan by a day or two. Link this to the prohibition of imitating the People of the Book. Understand how the dalīl applies to each scenario.
The hadith is the primary textual proof; its scope is extended by qiyās.
3
Analyze the practice of talawwum
Talawwum (delaying the intention until midday) is recommended. The passage states that for judges and muftis, fasting as a supererogatory act is better, but they should advise the common people to break.
The distinction rests on the ability to maintain a correct intention free from hesitation.
4
Distinguish between hesitation in essence and description
If the hesitation is in the essence (e.g., conditional: 'if it is Ramadan, I am fasting'), the intention is invalid. If the hesitation is in the description (e.g., 'for Ramadan if it is Ramadan, otherwise for qadā'), it is disliked but may be valid.
This distinction is unique to Hanafi fiqh and has practical consequences.
5
Apply the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is Imām Muhammad’s view: one should resolve on the night of doubt to fast for Ramadan if it is Ramadan, otherwise not to fast. This avoids both prohibition and loss of reward.
This view is stated as the madhhab of our companions in al-Fatāwā al-Ẓahīriyya.

ولهذا قالوا: ويفتوا بالصوم خاصتهم. وأما إذا ردد فإن كان في أصلها كأن نوی أن عن رمضان إن كان رمضان وإلا فليس بصائم وهذه غير صحيحة فليس بصائم. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية : وعن محمد ينبغي أن يعزم ليلة يوم الشك مكروه لتردده بين مكروهين، فإن ظهر أنه من رمضان أجزأه عنه وإلا كان تطوعاً غير مضمون بالإفساد ولا يكون عن الواجب لعدم الجزم به. والثانية إذا نوى أن يصوم عن رمضان إن كان منه وإلا فتطوع فهو مكروه لنية If it is equal, the extra is not required due to doubt, because its completion only becomes apparent when clear, but when cloudy it is not, unless it is said the original is clear and clouds are an accident and not considered before its realization. They only mentioned equality when clouds are realized and did not address the description of non-supererogatory fasting nor its description of permissibility and desirability. As for non-supererogatory fasting, if he is certain it is for Ramadan, it is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahriman) due to imitating the People of the Book because they increased in their fast, and upon this is carried the hadith prohibiting preceding with a fast of a day or two. And in its desirability if it coincides with his habitual fast, the correct view is it suffices if it becomes clear it is from Ramadan, otherwise it is a supererogatory fast not guaranteed by spoiling because it is in the sense of probable. If he is certain it is for another obligatory fast, it is lightly disliked (makruh tanzihan), the source of which is contrary to the better, because the prohibition is specific to the fast of Ramadan, but it is disliked due to the form of the prohibition carried upon Ramadan. If it becomes clear it is Ramadan, it suffices for it, as known if he was a resident, otherwise it suffices for what he intended, as if it becomes clear it is Sha'ban in the correct view. If he is certain it is supererogatory, there is no talk of its dislike, but there is disagreement on its desirability if it does not coincide with his fast. The better is to delay and not eat nor intend the fast until midday approaches, then if it approaches and the situation is not clear, they differed. Some said the better is to fast, some said to break. The general scholars hold that judges and muftis should fast supererogatorily and give that fatwa to their elite, and give fatwa to the common people to break. Muhammad ibn Salama and Abu Nasr said breaking is more precautionary because they agreed there is no sin on him if he breaks, and they differed on fasting; some said it is disliked and sinful. As in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya. Their statement 'he fasts' for the judge and mufti means he fasts who is able to control himself from vacillation in intention and observing that it is for the obligatory if tomorrow is Ramadan; for this they said: and they give fatwa of fasting to their elite. As for if he hesitates, if it is in its essence, like he intends that if it is Ramadan it is for Ramadan, otherwise he is not fasting, this is invalid and he is not fasting. In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya: from Muhammad it is recommended that he resolve on the night of the day of doubt that if tomorrow is Ramadan he is fasting for Ramadan, and if not from Ramadan then he is not fasting; this is the madhhab of our companions. And if he hesitates in its description, there are two forms: first: he intends to fast for Ramadan if tomorrow is from it, otherwise for another obligatory, this is disliked due to his hesitation between two disliked things. If it becomes clear it is from Ramadan, it suffices for it; otherwise it is supererogatory not guaranteed by spoiling, and it is not for the obligatory due to lack of certainty. Second: he intends to fast for Ramadan if it is from it, otherwise supererogatory; this is disliked due to the intention of the obligatory in one aspect. If it becomes clear it is from it, it suffices; otherwise it is supererogatory not guaranteed because of the inclusion of release in his determination in one aspect. His statement: ( And the general scholars that it is recommended etc. ) In al-Nahr: This indicates that delay is better for everyone, and whoever cannot resolve on the intention of supererogation is from the common people. There is reflection in this indication and the apparent of al-Hidayah contradicts it. His statement: (from vacillation in intention) i.e., hesitation in it, and he should have used 'في' instead of 'عن' as in al-Hidayah. In al-Nihaya: vacillation in intention is hesitation.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a detailed fiqh ruling on fasting the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk), i.e., the 30th of Sha'ban when there is uncertainty about the sighting of the crescent for Ramadan. The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains the various intentions a person may have and their legal consequences. The core ruling is that if one is certain it is for Ramadan, it is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahriman) because it imitates the People of the Book who added days to their fast, and the hadith prohibits preceding Ramadan by a day or two. However, if it coincides with a habitual fast (e.g., Mondays and Thursdays), it becomes mustahab and valid if it turns out to be Ramadan. If one intends another obligatory fast (e.g., a missed fast), it is lightly disliked (makruh tanzihan). If one intends supererogatory fasting, there is no dislike, but there is disagreement on its desirability. The better of the two views is to delay (talawwum) until midday. For judges and muftis, the preferred view is that they should fast supererogatorily and advise their elite to do so, but advise the common people to break, as they may not be able to control their intention. The passage also discusses hesitation in intention (taraddad). If the hesitation is in the essence (e.g., conditional intention), it is invalid. If the hesitation is in the description (e.g., intending for Ramadan if it is Ramadan, otherwise for another obligation or supererogation), it is disliked but may be valid if it turns out to be Ramadan. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the statement of Imam Muhammad that one should resolve on the night of doubt to fast for Ramadan if it is Ramadan, otherwise not to fast, which is the madhhab of our companions.

Key Terms
يوم الشك (yawm al-shakk): The 30th day of Sha'ban when it is uncertain whether the crescent for Ramadan has been sighted.
التلوم (al-talawwum): The recommended practice of delaying the intention to fast on the day of doubt until midday if the situation is unclear.
الترديد في النية (al-taraddad fi al-niyyah): Hesitation in the essence or description of the intention, which may render the fast invalid or disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person fasts on the day of doubt with the intention, 'I am fasting for Ramadan if tomorrow is Ramadan, otherwise I am not fasting'?
A) Valid, and it counts as a supererogatory fast if it turns out to be Sha'ban.
B) Disliked but valid if it becomes clear it is Ramadan.
C) Invalid because the intention is conditional (hesitation in essence).
D) Prohibitively disliked and invalid.

Key Takeaway
On the day of doubt, avoid certainty of Ramadan; instead, resolve to fast for Ramadan only if it is Ramadan, otherwise as a supererogatory fast—this is the mufta bihi position.

Fasting Before Ramadan: Habit vs. No Habit
Clarifies the ruling on fasting before Ramadan based on hadith and habit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on fasting a day or two before Ramadan, applying the exception for habitual fasts and distinguishing between intention and action.

Core Idea
Fasting before Ramadan is only disliked for the last day or two without a habit; a habitual fast removes the dislike.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on fasting immediately before Ramadan. The hadith 'Do not precede Ramadan by a fast of a day or two' is interpreted in light of the exception for those who have a regular fast. The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the distinction and resolves apparent contradictions between the hadith and the practice of connecting Sha'ban with Ramadan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling categories
Determine who has a habit of fasting (e.g., Monday/Thursday) and who does not. The ruling differs: with habit, no dislike; without habit, one or two days before is makruh tahrimi.
The habit can be any regular fast, not necessarily a specific day.
2
Understand the hadith and its apparent prohibition
The hadith 'Do not precede Ramadan by a fast of a day or two' seems to prohibit all fasting before Ramadan. But the exception 'unless it coincides with a fast he used to fast' modifies the ruling.
The prohibition is not absolute; it targets those without a habit.
3
Apply the exception for habitual fasts
If the day before Ramadan coincides with a person's regular fast, the dislike is removed. The text also clarifies that three or more days are not disliked, even without a habit.
The day of doubt (30th Sha'ban) when fasted as supererogation is also not disliked.
4
Distinguish intention from action
Some scholars interpret the hadith as forbidding the intention of Ramadan, not the act of fasting itself. Thus, fasting as nafl is permissible.
This interpretation removes the dislike entirely for supererogatory fasts.
5
Note the ruling on the day of doubt
Fasting the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk) with the intention of nafl is not disliked, according to the relied-upon position.
This is an important distinction from the general ruling on the last day or two.

ولم يتعرض المصنف لصوم ما قبله وصرح في الكافي بأنه إن وافق الشك صوماً يوم كان يصومه فالصوم أفضل وكذا إن صام كله أو نصفه أو ثلاثة من أخره، ولم يقيد بكون الثلاثة عادة. وصرح في التحفة بكراهة الصوم قبل رمضان بيوم أو يومين لمن ليس له عادة لقوله عليه السلام لا تتقدموا رمضان بصوم يوم الا أو يومين إلا أن يوافق صوماً كان يصومه أحدكم» وإنما كره خوفاً من أن يظن أنه زيادة على رمضان إذا اعتادوا ذلك . فالحاصل أن من له عادة فلا كراهة في حقه مطلقاً، ومن ليس له عادة فلا كراهة في التقدم بثلاثة فأكثر ويكره في اليوم واليومين. وأما صوم الشك فلا يكره بنية التطوع مطلقاً . قوله: (ومن رأى هلال رمضان أو الفطر ورد قوله صام فإن أفطر قضى فقط) لقوله تعالى في هلال رمضان فمن شهد منكم الشهر فليصمه ﴾ [البقرة : ١٨٥] وهذا قد شهده. والحديث في هلال الفطر «صومكم يوم تصومون وفطركم يوم تفطرون» والناس لم يفطروا فيها وإن لا ينها من ضجع في الأمر إذا وهي فيه وقصر. كذا في المغرب قوله : (ويكره في اليوم واليومين) مقتضى ما مر من حمل حديث النهي عن التقدم بيوم . أو يومين على أنه من رمضان عدم الكراهة، وممن صرح بحمل الحديث على ذلك صاحب الهداية ،وشراحها وظاهر ما مر عن التحفة خلافه وفي الشرنبلالية قال في الفوائد والمراد بقوله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم لا تقدموا الخ» التقديم على قصد أن يكون من رمضان لأن التقديم بالشيء على الشيء أن ينوي به قبل حسنه وأوانه ووقته وزمانه وشعبان وقت التطوع، فإذا صام عن شعبان لم يأت بصوم رمضان قبل زمانه وأوانه فلا يكون هذا تقدماً عليه ا.هـ. كذا بخط أستاذي رحمه الله تعالى. وبهذا تنتفى كراهة صوم الشك تطوعاً اه كلام الشرنبلالية. وفي المعراج عن الإيضاح: لا بأس بصوم يوم أو يومين أو ثلاثة قبل رمضان أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يصل شعبان ،برمضان والمراد بقوله «لا تتقدموا الحديث» يصير زيادة على الفرض وفي العناية وغيرها : فإن قيل فما فائدة قوله ذلك كذلك؟ أجيب بأن يوماً ويومين ما وصل إلى حد الكثرة فيجوز أنه يتوهم بأن القليل معفو فيجوز كما في كثير من الأحكام فنفى ذلك. وفي السعدية : يجوز أن يجاب بأن المحتمل هو التقدم بيوم أو يومين كما هو الواقع من الممارسين بعلم حساب النجوم
And the author did not address the fast before it, and it was stated in al-Kafi that if the doubt coincides with a fast he used to fast, then fasting is better, similarly if he fasts all of it, or half of it, or three from its end, and he did not restrict the three to being a habit. And it was stated in al-Tuhfa that fasting before Ramadan by a day or two is disliked for one who has no habit, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Do not precede Ramadan by a fast of a day or two, unless it coincides with a fast that one of you used to fast.' It is disliked for fear that it be thought an increase to Ramadan if they become accustomed to that. So the conclusion is that one who has a habit has no dislike absolutely, and one who has no habit has no dislike in preceding by three or more, and it is disliked in the day or two. As for the fast of doubt, it is not disliked with the intention of supererogation absolutely. His statement: (And whoever sees the crescent of Ramadan or Eid and his testimony is rejected, he fasts, and if he breaks he only makes up) due to His statement regarding the crescent of Ramadan: 'So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it' [2:185], and he has witnessed it. And the hadith regarding the crescent of Eid: 'Your fast is the day you fast, and your breaking is the day you break,' and the people did not break on that day... So in al-Mughrib: His statement: (It is disliked in the day or two) the implication of what passed of carrying the hadith of prohibition of preceding by a day or two as being for Ramadan is that there is no dislike. And among those who stated the carrying of the hadith on that is the author of al-Hidayah and its commentators. And the apparent of what passed from al-Tuhfa is contrary to it. In al-Sharnabaliyya it is said in al-Fawa'id: The meaning of his statement (peace be upon him) 'do not precede' etc. is preceding with the intention that it be from Ramadan, because preceding a thing with a thing means intending it before its beauty, time, and season. Sha'ban is the time for supererogation. So if he fasts for Sha'ban, he has not performed the fast of Ramadan before its time and season, so this is not a preceding upon it. By this the dislike of fasting the day of doubt as supererogation is removed. So the words of al-Sharnabaliyya. In al-Mi'raj from al-Idah: There is no harm in fasting a day or two or three before Ramadan because he (peace be upon him) used to connect Sha'ban with Ramadan. The meaning of his statement 'do not precede' the hadith is that it becomes an increase on the obligatory. In al-Inaya and others: If it is said, what is the benefit of his statement like that? The answer is that a day or two have not reached the limit of abundance, so it is possible that it would be thought that the small amount is excused and permissible as in many rulings, so he negated that. In al-Sa'diyya: It is permissible to answer that the probable is the precedence by a day or two as is the practice of those familiar with the science of stars.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on fasting before Ramadan. The author notes that al-Kafi states that if the day of doubt coincides with a habitual fast, fasting is better. If one fasts the entire month of Sha'ban or half or three days at the end, it is also allowed, but al-Tuhfa states that fasting a day or two before Ramadan is disliked for those without a habit, based on the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The reason is to avoid the suspicion of adding to Ramadan. The conclusion: for those with a habit (e.g., fasting Mondays and Thursdays), there is no dislike. For those without, fasting three or more days before is not disliked, but fasting one or two days is disliked. However, fasting the day of doubt as supererogation is not disliked at all. The passage then moves to the ruling on seeing the crescent and having testimony rejected: such a person must fast, and if he breaks, he only makes up (qada). The proof is the Quranic verse and the hadith. There is also discussion of the interpretation of the hadith 'Do not precede...' Some scholars interpret it as forbidding the intention of Ramadan, not the fast itself. Thus, if one fasts as supererogation, it is not included in the prohibition. This removes the dislike for fasting the day of doubt with the intention of supererogation.

Key Terms
يوم الشك (yawm al-shakk): The day of doubt (30th Sha'ban) when it is uncertain whether the crescent is sighted.
عادة (ʿādah): A habitual fast, e.g., regularly fasting on Mondays and Thursdays, or any other consistent voluntary fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it not disliked to fast a day before Ramadan?
A) For someone who has a habit of fasting on that day.
B) For someone who intends it as part of Ramadan.
C) For someone who is traveling.
D) It is always disliked.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits fasting before Ramadan when it coincides with a habit or when it is three or more days, but dislikes it for one or two days without habit.
