قوله : ( وقبل بعلة خبر عدل ولو قنا أو أثنى لرمضان وحرين أو حر وحرتين للفطر) لأن صوم رمضان أمر ديني فأشبه رواية الإخبار ولهذا لا يختص بلفظ الشهادة خلافاً لشيخ الإسلام. ولا يشترط الدعوى لكن قال في الفتاوي الظهيرية أنه قولهما، أما على قول الإمام أبي حنيفة فينبغي أن يشترط الدعوى، أما في شهادة الفطر والأضحى فيشترط لفظ الشهادة وتشترط العدالة في الكل لأن قول الفاسق في الديانات التي يمكن تلقيها من العدول غيره مقبول كالهلال ورواية الأخبار ولو تعدد كفاسقين فأكثر . كذا في الولوالجية بخلاف ما يتيسر تلقيه منهم حيث يتحرى في خبر الفاسق كالإخبار بطهارة الماء ونجاسته وحل الطعام وحرمته وبخلاف الهدية والوكالة وما لا إلزام فيه من المعاملات حيث يقبل خبره بدون التحري للزوم الضرورة ولا دليل سواه فوجب قبوله مطلقاً. وحقيقة العدالة ملكة تحمل على ملازمة التقوى والمروءة والشرط أدناها وهو ترك الكبائر والإصرار على الصغائر وما يخل بالمروءة كما عرف تحقيقه في تعريف الأصول، فلزم أن يكون مسلماً عاقلاً بالغاً، وأما الحرية والبصر وعدم الحد في قذف وعدم الولاء والعداوة فمختص بالشهادة. وعن أبي حنيفة نفي رواية المحدود والظاهر خلافه لقبول رواية أبي بكرة بعد ما تاب وكان قد حد في قذف، وأما مجهول الحال وهو المستور فعن أبي حنيفة قبوله وظاهر الرواية عدمه لأن المراد بالعدل في ظاهر الرواية من ثبتت عدالته وأن الحكم بقوله فرع ثبوتها ولا ثبوت في المستور، وما ذكره الطحاوي من عدم اشتراط العدالة فمحمول على قبول المستور الذي هو إحدى الروايتين، وصحح البزازي في فتاواه قبول المستور وهو خلاف ظاهر الرواية كما علمت، أما مع تبين الفسق فلا قائل به عندنا وفرعوا عليه ما لو شهدوا في تاسع عشرين رمضان أنهم رأوا هلال رمضان قبل صومهم بيوم إن كانوا في هذا المصر لا تقبل شهادتهم لأنهم تركوا الحسبة، وإن جاؤوا من خارج قبلت وفي البزازية : الفاسق إذا رآه وحده يشهد لأن القاضي ربما يقبل شهادته لكن القاضي يرده ا هـ . وأما هلال الفطر فلأنه تعلق به نفع العباد وهو الفطر فأشبه سائر حقوقهم فيشترط فيه ما يشترط في سائر حقوقهم من العدالة والحرية والعدد وعدم الحد في قذف ولفظ الشهادة والدعوى على خلاف فيه إن أمكن ذلك وإلا فقد تقدم
تأمل قوله : (وفي الفطران أخبر عدلان برؤية الهلال قال في الشرنبلالية: أي وبالسماء علة قوله : وفيها أيضاً وإذا صام الخ ذكر في الذخيرة : وإن صام أهل المصر بغير رؤية من غير عد شعبان ثلاثين وفيهم رجل لم يصم معهم حتى رأوا الهلال من الغد فصام أهل المصر ثلاثين وصام هذا الرجل تسعة وعشرين يوماً فليس عليه قضاء اه تأمل قوله : (لأنهم تركوا الحسبة) فإن شاهد يوم البحر الرائق ج ٢ م ٣٠
أنهم لو كانوا في بلدة لا قاضي فيها ولا زوال فإن الناس يصومون بقول الثقة ويفطرون بإخبار عدلين للضرورة.
،
وأطلقه فشمل ما لو كان المخبر من مصر أو جاء من خارجه وهو ظاهر الرواية خلافاً للإمام الفضلي حيث قال : إنما يقبل الواحد العدل إذا فسر وقال رأيته خارج البلد في الصحراء أو يقول رأيته في البلدة من بين خلل السحاب أما بدون هذا التفسير فلا يقبل، كذا في الظهيرية. وأشار إلى أنه يقبل في هلال رمضان شهادة واحد عدل على شهادة واحد عدل بخلاف الشهادة على الشهادة في سائر الأحكام حيث لا تقبل ما لم يشهد على شهادة رجل واحد رجلان أو رجل وامرأتان لما ذكرنا أنه من باب الأخبار لا من باب الشهادة. كذا في البدائع، وكذا تقبل فيه شهادة العبد على العبد كذا في البزازية، وكذا شهادة المرأة على المرأة كذا في الظهيرية. وإلى أنهم لو صاموا بشهادة واحد وغم هلال شوّال فإنهم لا يفطرون فتثبت الرمضانية بشهادته لا الفطر خلافاً لما روي عند محمد أنهم يفطرون وصححه في غاية البيان. وأما إذا صاموا بشهادة اثنين فإنهم يفطرون اتفاقاً كذا في البدائع. وحكى البزازي فيه خلافاً والعلة غيم أو غبار أو نحوهما هنا. وفي الأصول الخارج المتعلق بالحكم المؤثر فيه،
الحسبة إذا أخر شهادته بلا عذر يفسق ولا تقبل شهادته كما في الأشباه والنظائر قوله : (وإلى أنهم لو صاموا بشهادة واحدة الخ) قال في النهر : ثم إذا قبلت وأكملوا العدة ولم ير روى الحسن عن الإمام وهو قول الثاني أنهم يفطرون وسئل عنه محمد فقال : يثبت الفطر بحكم القاضي لا بقول الواحد . وفي غاية البيان : وقول محمد أصح. قال الشارح والأشبه أن يقال : إن كانت السماء مصحية لا يفطرون لظهور غلطه وإن كانت مغيمة يفطرون لعدم ظهوره، ولو ثبت برجلين أفطروا، وعن السعدي لا وهكذا عن مجموع النوازل قال في الفتح : ولو قيل إن قبلهما في الصحو لا يفطرون وفي الغيم افطروا لم يبعد. وفي السراج صاموا بشاهدين افطروا عند كمال العدة إجماعاً. وهذا ظاهر فيما إذا كانت متغيمة عند الفطر، أما لو كانت مصحية ينبغي أن لا يفطروا كما لو شهدوا الساعة ا هـ . لكن في الإمداد صحح في الدراية والخلاصة والبزازية حل الفطر، وذكر في متنه أنه لا خلاف في حل الفطر إذا كان بالسماء علة، ولو ثبت رمضان بشهادة الفرد وذكر أن ما مر عن السعدي حكاه عنه في التجنيس فيما إذا كانت السماء مصحية وذكر عن الحلواني أن الخلاف في مسألة ما لو ثبت بشهادة واحد إذا كانت مصحية وإلا أفطروا بلا خلاف ا.هـ. فصار الحاصل على هذا ما ذكره في نور الإيضاح إذا تم العدد بشهادة فرد ولم ير هلال الفطر والسماء مصحية لا يحل الفطر، واختلف الترجيح فيما إذا كان بشهادة عدلين ولا خلاف في حل الفطر إذا كان بالسماء علة. ولو ثبت رمضان بشهادة الفرد قال في شرحه وقوله في غاية البيان «قول محمد هو الأصح» يحمل على ما قال الكمال منهم من استحسن في الصحو المروي عن الحسن من أنهم لا يفطرون وفي الغيم أخذ بقول محمد ا.هـ. وحينئذ فلا يخالف ما مر عن الحلواني والله تعالى أعلم.
His saying: (And with an excuse, the news of a just person is accepted, even if a slave or a woman, for Ramadan, and two free men or one free man and two free women for the breaking of the fast) because the fast of Ramadan is a religious matter, so it resembles the narration of reports, and for this reason it is not restricted to the word of testimony, contrary to the Shaykh of Islam. And a claim is not required, but in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya it is said that it is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa, a claim should be required. As for the testimony for the breaking (al-fitr) and the sacrifice (al-adha), the word of testimony is required, and justice is required in all, because the word of a sinner in religious matters that can be received from just others is accepted, like the crescent and narration of reports, even if they are many, like two sinners or more. Thus in al-Walwaljiyya, contrary to what can be easily received from them where one investigates the news of a sinner, like reporting the purity of water and its impurity, and the permissibility and prohibition of food, and contrary to the gift and agency and what has no compulsion from transactions, where his news is accepted without investigation due to necessity and no other evidence, so its acceptance is obligatory absolutely. The reality of justice is a disposition that leads to constant piety and chivalry, and the condition is the minimum of it, which is abandoning major sins and persistence in minor sins and what detracts from chivalry, as its verification is known in the definition of principles. So it is necessary that he be Muslim, sane, and adult. As for freedom, sight, not being subject to hadd punishment for slander, and not having loyalty or enmity, they are specific to testimony. From Abu Hanifa: the rejection of the narration of the one who has been flogged, but the apparent is contrary to it, due to the acceptance of the narration of Abu Bakra after he repented, and he had been flogged for slander. As for the unknown status, which is the mastur, from Abu Hanifa his acceptance, and the apparent of the riwaya is its non-acceptance, because the meaning of 'just' in the apparent riwaya is one whose justice is established, and the judgement by his statement is a branch of its establishment, and there is no establishment for the mastur. And what al-Tahawi mentioned of not requiring justice is interpreted as acceptance of the mastur, which is one of the two narrations. And al-Bazzazi in his Fatawa corroborated acceptance of the mastur, and it is contrary to the apparent riwaya as you know. As for when immorality is evident, there is no proponent of it among us. And they derived from it: if they testify on the 29th of Ramadan that they saw the crescent of Ramadan a day before their fast, if they were in this city, their testimony is not accepted because they left the duty (hisha). If they came from outside, it is accepted. In al-Bazzaziyya: The sinner, if he sees it alone, testifies, because the judge might accept his testimony, but the judge rejects it. As for the crescent of the breaking (al-fitr), because the benefit of the servants is attached to it, which is the breaking, so it resembles their other rights. Thus what is required in their other rights is required therein: justice, freedom, number, not being subject to hadd for slander, the word of testimony, and a claim, with a difference of opinion therein if possible; otherwise it has already preceded. Ponder his saying: (And concerning the breaking, if two just persons inform of the sighting of the crescent) He said in al-Sharnablaliyya: meaning and with the sky being overcast. His saying: And in it also, if they fast... mentioned in al-Dhakhira: If the people of the city fast without a sighting, without counting Sha'ban as thirty, and there is a man who did not fast with them until they saw the crescent the next day, so the people of the city fasted thirty and this man fasted twenty-nine days, there is no make-up upon him. Ponder his saying: (because they left the duty [hisha]) for the witness on that day... al-Bahr al-Ra'iq vol. 2 p. 30. That if they were in a town where there is no judge and no [call to prayer?], the people fast on the word of a trustworthy person and break fast on the information of two just persons due to necessity. And he made it absolute, so it includes whether the informant is from the city or comes from outside, and that is the apparent riwaya, contrary to Imam al-Fadli where he said: Acceptable only if he explains and says 'I saw it outside the city in the desert' or 'I saw it in the city through an opening in the clouds'; without this explanation it is not accepted. Thus in al-Zahiriyya. And it indicates that for the crescent of Ramadan, the testimony of one just person upon the testimony of one just person is accepted, contrary to testimony upon testimony in other rulings, where it is not accepted unless two men or one man and two women testify upon the testimony of one man, because it is from the category of reports, not testimony. Thus in al-Bada'i'. Likewise, the testimony of a slave upon a slave is accepted in it; thus in al-Bazzaziyya. Likewise, the testimony of a woman upon a woman; thus in al-Zahiriyya. And that if they fast on the testimony of one and the crescent of Shawwal is obscured, they do not break fast; the Ramadan is established by his testimony, not the breaking, contrary to what is narrated from Muhammad that they break fast, and he corrected it in Ghayat al-Bayan. And if they fast on the testimony of two, they break fast by agreement; thus in al-Bada'i'. And al-Bazzazi narrated a difference of opinion therein, and the obstacle (illa) is clouds, dust, or the like here. And in al-Usul: the external matter related to the effective cause therein. Hisha: if he delays his testimony without an excuse, he becomes immoral and his testimony is not accepted, as in al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir. His saying: (And that if they fast on the testimony of one...) He said in al-Nahr: Then if it is accepted and they complete the count and do not see, al-Hasan narrated from the Imam (Abu Hanifa) that they break fast, and it is the statement of the second (Muhammad?); he was asked about it and Muhammad said: The breaking is established by the judge's ruling, not by the word of one. In Ghayat al-Bayan: The statement of Muhammad is more correct. The commentator said: The more appropriate is to say: if the sky is clear, they do not break fast due to the apparent error; if it is cloudy, they break fast due to the lack of apparent error. If it is established by two men, they break fast. From al-Sa'di: no; and likewise from Majmu' al-Nawazil. He said in al-Fath: And if it were said that acceptance of them in clear weather they do not break fast and in clouds they break fast, it would not be far-fetched. In al-Siraj: They fasted on the testimony of two; they break fast upon completion of the count by consensus. This is apparent when it is overcast at the time of breaking; if it is clear, it is better that they do not break fast, as if they testified at the hour. But in al-Imdad, he corrected in al-Diraya, al-Khulasa, and al-Bazzaziyya: it is permissible to break fast. He mentioned in its matn that there is no difference in the permissibility of breaking fast if there is an obstacle in the sky. And if Ramadan is established by the testimony of one, and he mentioned that what is from al-Sa'di is narrated from him in al-Tajnis when the sky is clear, and from al-Halwani that the difference is in the issue if it is established by the testimony of one when it is clear; otherwise they break fast without difference. So the result according to this is what is mentioned in Nur al-Idah: if the count is completed by the testimony of one and he does not see the crescent of breaking and the sky is clear, it is not permissible to break fast. And the weighting differs when it is by the testimony of two, and there is no difference in the permissibility of breaking fast if there is an obstacle in the sky. And if Ramadan is established by the testimony of one, he said in his commentary: And his saying in Ghayat al-Bayan 'the statement of Muhammad is more correct' is interpreted as what al-Kamal said: they approved in clear weather the narration from al-Hasan that they do not break fast, and in clouds they adopt the statement of Muhammad. Then it does not contradict what is from al-Halwani. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the conditions for accepting witnesses for the crescent of Ramadan and Shawwal. The matn (Kanz al-Daqaiq) states that with an excuse (like clouds), the report of one just person, even a slave or woman, is accepted for Ramadan; for Shawwal, two free men or one free man and two free women are required. The commentary explains the rationale: Ramadan is a religious matter (أمر ديني) akin to narrating hadith, so it does not require the formal wording of testimony (شهادة), unlike financial matters. The opposing view of al-Shafi'i (شيخ الإسلام) is noted, as he requires two witnesses for Ramadan. Within the Hanafi school, there is a difference between Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on whether a claim (دعوى) is required for Ramadan; Abu Hanifa requires it, while the others do not. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that a claim is not required. The passage then defines justice (عدالة) as leaving major sins and not persisting in minor sins, and states that the witness must be Muslim, sane, and adult. Freedom, sight, etc. are only required for testimony (شهادة) in other matters, not for reporting the crescent. The acceptance of the مستور (person of unknown justice) is debated: the apparent riwaya rejects it, but some scholars like al-Bazzazi accept it. The text then distinguishes between Ramadan and Shawwal: since Shawwal involves the benefit of breaking the fast (حق العباد), it requires the stricter conditions of testimony (عدد, حرية, etc.). The commentary also discusses cases when the sky is clear (مصحية) vs. overcast (مغيمة) and the differing views on whether to break fast when Ramadan is established by one witness. The preferred view distinguishes: if clear, do not break fast due to obvious error; if overcast, break fast. The discussion ends with a harmonization of various authorities.

Key Terms
مصحية (mushiah): clear sky without clouds or obstacles; in this context, indicates that the crescent should be visible if present.
مغيمة (mutaghayyima): cloudy or overcast sky; an obstacle that may prevent sighting even if the crescent exists.
علة (illa): excuse or obstacle (e.g., clouds, dust) that prevents clear sighting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the lesson, what should a community do if they completed 30 days of fasting based on one witness, the sky is clear, and no crescent is seen?
A) Break fast immediately because 30 days have passed.
B) Do not break fast and treat it as still Ramadan.
C) Break fast only if a judge rules it.
D) Break fast and then make up a day later.

Key Takeaway
When Ramadan is established by one witness and the sky is clear, the community must not break fast on the 30th night; they should continue fasting until certainty.

Testimony for the Crescents: One Witness for Ramadan, Two for Shawwal
Discussion on when one witness suffices for Ramadan and two for Shawwal, and disputes about cloudy sky.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of witnesses required for sighting Ramadan and Shawwal crescents, and differentiate between clear and cloudy sky cases in the dispute over breaking the fast.

Core Idea
One just witness suffices for Ramadan but not for Shawwal; the sky condition determines the ruling on breaking the fast.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, the author unpacks the Hanafi rules for accepting testimony for crescent sightings. He navigates an intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad on whether a single witness for Ramadan can also establish its end when the sky is cloudy. The discussion reveals the interplay between the nature of testimony (ikhbar vs shahada) and external factors like weather.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base rule for testimony in a town without a judge
The passage begins by stating that in a town with no judge or proper noon time, people fast on the word of one trustworthy person and break the fast on the report of two just persons out of necessity. This establishes the default: one witness for Ramadan, two for Shawwal.
This is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah).
2
Understand the special status of Ramadan crescent as ikhbar
The author explains that testimony for Ramadan is treated as mere report (ikhbar), not formal testimony (shahada). Therefore, testimony upon testimony (shahada 'ala shahada) from one person is accepted, as are testimonies from slaves and women.
This distinguishes hilal cases from other legal testimonies.
3
Locate the dispute on breaking fast after one witness
The core dispute: if people fasted on the testimony of one just person for Ramadan and the Shawwal crescent is not sighted, do they break the fast? Abu Hanifa says no (the one witness only proves the start), while Imam Muhammad says yes (they break). Later scholars reconcile this based on sky condition.
Al-Kamal and the commentator prefer the reconciliation.
4
Examine the reconciliation based on sky condition
If the sky is clear (mushiyya), error is apparent, so they do not break the fast. If the sky is cloudy (mugheema), error is hidden, so they break the fast. This reconciles the two positions.
This is the mufta bihi (operative ruling).
5
Note the consensus when two witnesses testify
If fasting was based on two witnesses, they break the fast by consensus (ittifaqan), though some narrations qualify this based on sky condition. The passage notes that if the sky is clear, even two witnesses should be questioned.
The default for Shawwal remains two witnesses.

بشهادة واحد إذا كانت مصحية وإلا أفطروا بلا خلاف ا.هـ. فصار الحاصل على هذا ما ذكره في نور الإيضاح إذا تم العدد بشهادة فرد ولم ير هلال الفطر والسماء مصحية لا يحل الفطر، واختلف الترجيح فيما إذا كان If they are in a town with no judge and no noon (to determine time), then the people fast on the statement of a trustworthy person and break the fast on the report of two just persons out of necessity. And it was left general, so it includes whether the informant is from the city or comes from outside, and that is the apparent narration, contrary to Imam al-Fadli who said: The single just person is only accepted if he explains and says 'I saw it outside the city in the desert' or says 'I saw it in the city from between gaps in the clouds'; but without this explanation, it is not accepted. Thus in al-Zahiriya. And it indicated that for the crescent of Ramadan, the testimony of one just person upon the testimony of one just person is accepted, unlike testimony upon testimony in other rulings where it is not accepted unless two men or a man and two women testify upon the testimony of one man, because we mentioned that it is from the category of reports, not from the category of testimony. Thus in al-Bada'i. Likewise, the testimony of a slave upon a slave is accepted, thus in al-Bazzaziyya, and likewise the testimony of a woman upon a woman, thus in al-Zahiriya. And that if they fasted on the testimony of one and the crescent of Shawwal is obscured, they do not break the fast; thus Ramadan is established by his testimony, not breaking the fast, contrary to what is narrated from Muhammad that they break the fast, and it was corrected in Ghayat al-Bayan. But if they fasted on the testimony of two, they break the fast by agreement, thus in al-Bada'i. Al-Bazzazi reported a disagreement about it, and the cause is clouds, dust, or the like here. And in the principles, the external factor related to the effective cause of the ruling; if a person delays his testimony without excuse, he becomes immoral and his testimony is not accepted, as in al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir. His saying: (And that if they fasted on one testimony, etc.) He said in al-Nahr: Then if it is accepted and they complete the count and do not see (the crescent), al-Hasan narrated from the Imam that it is the second saying that they break the fast, and Muhammad was asked about it and said: Breaking the fast is established by the judge's ruling, not by the statement of one. And in Ghayat al-Bayan: Muhammad's statement is more correct. The commentator said: The more appropriate is to say: If the sky is clear, they do not break the fast due to the apparentness of his error; but if it is cloudy, they break the fast due to the lack of its apparentness. And if it is established by two men, they break the fast; and from al-Sa'di, no, and likewise from Majmu' al-Nawazil. Al-Fath said: If it were said that accepting them in clear weather they do not break the fast and in clouds they break the fast, it would not be far. And in al-Siraj: They fasted with two witnesses; they break the fast upon completion of the count by consensus. This is apparent when it is cloudy at the time of breaking the fast; but if it is clear, it is appropriate that they do not break the fast, as if they testified at the hour. End. But in al-Imdad, it was corrected in al-Diraya, al-Khulasa, and al-Bazzaziyya that breaking the fast is permissible, and it was mentioned in its text that there is no dispute about the permissibility of breaking the fast if there is a condition in the sky. And if Ramadan is established by a single person's testimony, he mentioned that what passed from al-Sa'di, he narrated it from him in al-Tajnis as being when the sky is clear, and he mentioned from al-Halwani that the dispute is about the case when it is established by one witness if the sky is clear; otherwise, they break the fast without dispute. So the result based on this is what was mentioned in Nur al-Idah: If the count is completed by a single testimony and the crescent of breaking the fast is not seen and the sky is clear, breaking the fast is not permissible; and the preference differs when it is with two just witnesses, and there is no dispute about the permissibility of breaking the fast if there is a condition in the sky. And if Ramadan is established by a single person's testimony, he said in his commentary: His statement in Ghayat al-Bayan 'Muhammad's statement is more correct' is interpreted as what al-Kamal said: some of them considered it good in clear weather from what is narrated from al-Hasan that they do not break the fast, and in clouds they adopt Muhammad's statement. Thus it does not contradict what passed from al-Halwani. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq deals with the acceptance of testimony for sighting the crescents of Ramadan and Shawwal. It begins by stating that in a town without a judge or proper knowledge of noon, people may rely on a trustworthy person for fasting and need two just persons for breaking the fast out of necessity. The comment 'wa utliqa' indicates that this ruling applies whether the informant is from the town or outside. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam al-Fadli requires the single witness to specify that he saw the crescent outside the city or through gaps in the clouds; otherwise, his testimony is not accepted. The text then explains that for Ramadan, one just witness suffices based on the principle that it is a matter of 'ikhbar' (report) rather than formal testimony, so testimony upon testimony is accepted even from one person, unlike other cases where two are needed. It also acknowledges that the testimony of a slave or a woman is accepted for this purpose. A key dispute arises when people fast based on one witness for Ramadan and then the Shawwal crescent is not sighted: the Hanafi position (supported by Abu Hanifa) is that they do not break the fast, because the one witness establishes only the beginning of Ramadan, not its end. This is contrary to a narration from Muhammad that they do break the fast, though some later scholars like al-Kamal prefer Abu Hanifa's view when the sky is clear and Muhammad's when cloudy. The text then discusses the difference of opinion when two witnesses testify: generally they break the fast, but if the sky is clear and their testimony is later shown to be erroneous, they should not break the fast. The commentator reconciles these views by considering the condition of the sky: if clear, errors are apparent, so the fast is not broken; if cloudy, errors are hidden, so breaking is allowed. The passage concludes that there is no disagreement about breaking the fast when there is an excuse (like clouds).

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Testimony; in this context, it refers to the report of a sighting of the crescent.
عدل (adl): Just person; someone whose testimony is acceptable due to probity.
غيم (ghaym): Clouds that may obscure the crescent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If people in a town fasted based on one just witness's testimony for Ramadan, and then the Shawwal crescent is not sighted with a clear sky, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) They must break the fast immediately because Ramadan is over.
B) They do not break the fast because the one witness does not establish the end of Ramadan.
C) They break the fast only if the judge orders it.
D) They fast an additional day to be cautious.

Key Takeaway
One just witness suffices to begin Ramadan, but two are needed for Shawwal unless the sky is cloudy, in which case the same witness can also establish the end.

The Testimony of a Secluded Girl for Ramadan Crescent and Classification of Witness Requirements
States ruling for jariyah and general witness conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a secluded virgin's testimony for Ramadan crescent and classify witness requirements across different categories (deenyat, huquq al-ibad, etc.) with exceptions.

Core Idea
A secluded girl must testify for Ramadan crescent without permission; witness requirements vary by category: religious matters need one just witness, pure rights need two, with exceptions.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a specific scenario: a secluded virgin seeing the Ramadan crescent on a cloudy night. It rules that she must go out and testify without her guardian's permission. Then it expands to a broader legal taxonomy: how the conditions for witness testimony vary depending on whether the case involves religious duties, people's rights, matters of obligation, or matters that men cannot access. Understanding this classification is essential for correctly applying Hanafi laws of testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific ruling
The passage first states a specific case: a jariyah mukhaddarah (secluded virgin) sees the crescent of Ramadan when the sky is cloudy. What is the ruling?
The ruling is that she must go out and testify without asking permission from her guardians.
2
Understand the basis in deenyat
Why is this testimony accepted from a single secluded girl? Because it falls under the category of deenyat (religious matters), where a single trustworthy report suffices.
Examples of deenyat include sighting of Ramadan crescent, matters of faith, and other purely religious obligations.
3
Explore the general classification of witness requirements
The passage then lists categories: deenyat (one witness), huquq al-ibad (two witnesses with conditions), matters with no obligation (discernment enough), matters with partial obligation (agent/messenger).
Pay attention to the conditions: number, uprightness, wording, and special exemptions.
4
Apply exceptions
Note exceptions: if the obligated party is non-Muslim, Islam is not required in the witness; for hidden matters (virginity, childbirth), number and masculinity are not required.
These exceptions show that the law adapts to practical needs.
5
Note intra-madhhab differences
The phrase 'عندهما' refers to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) who differ from Imam Abu Hanifa on cases like dismissal of an agent. Imam stipulated uprightness or number.
These differences affect the practical ruling in those specific sub-cases.

And he [the author] indicated that the secluded virgin, if she sees the crescent of Ramadan and there is an obstruction in the sky, it is obligatory upon her to go out that night and testify without the permission of her guardians, as clarified by al-Bazzazi. And know that whatever is from the category of religious matters, a single trustworthy person's report is sufficient for it, like the crescent of Ramadan. And whatever is from the rights of people and involves pure obligation, like sales and property, its condition is number (of witnesses) and uprightness and the wording of testimony with its other conditions. And from that [category] is [testimony about] breaking the fast, unless the one obligated is not Muslim, then Islam is not required in the witness. And also what men do not have knowledge of, like virginity, childbirth, and defects in the private parts, there is no condition of number or masculinity. And what has no obligation involved, like informing about agencies, mudarabahs, permission for trade, messages in gifts, and partnerships, then there is no condition except discernment with verification of the heart. And what involves obligation from one aspect, like the dismissal of an agent, sequestration of a permitted person, dissolution of a partnership and mudaraba, then the messenger and agent in that are as before them according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Imam (Abu Hanifa) stipulated his uprightness or number, as known in Tahrir al-Usul.

Key Terms
الجارية المخدرة (al-jariyah al-mukhaddarah): a secluded virgin who does not go out in public
خبر الواحد العدل (khabar al-wahid al-'adl): report of a single trustworthy person, sufficient in religious matters
الديانات (al-deenyat): matters of religion, where one witness suffices

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats testimony for Ramadan crescent as a religious duty where a single just witness suffices, even a secluded girl without permission.

Qada' for Uncertain Month Counts: The Bukhara Case
Historical case and derivation of qada' rules.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the required number of qada' days when Ramadan's length is uncertain due to missing crescent sightings, by identifying how Shaban was counted.

Core Idea
When Ramadan's start is uncertain, makeup days depend on how many previous months were counted without sighting.

This lesson examines a famous historical case from Bukhara where the start of Ramadan was uncertain due to disputed crescent sightings. The Hanafi jurists derived precise rules for qada' when the count of days is in doubt. We will follow the reasoning step by step through multiple scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial situation
The people began fasting on Wednesday, but on the 29th day two or three witnesses claimed to have seen the crescent on Tuesday night, making Wednesday the 30th. Determine whether the sky was clear or obstructed.
If the sky was clear, the fast was only 28 days; if obstructed, they continued to Thursday.
2
Determine the actual days fasted
In the scenario discussed, the community fasted only 28 days of Ramadan. This is the baseline for calculating qada'.
If they had fasted 29 days, no qada' is required.
3
Analyze how Shaban was counted
The number of qada' days depends on whether the crescent of Shaban was seen and whether Shaban was completed as 30 days with or without sighting.
Three possibilities: (a) Shaban crescent seen and counted 30, (b) Shaban not seen but counted 30, (c) Shaban crescent seen but counted 29 (fasted 29).
4
Apply the corresponding qada' rule
If Shaban crescent was seen and counted 30, qada' is one day. If Shaban was counted 30 without sighting, qada' is two days. If no sighting at all and count uncertain, qada' may increase.
The reasoning: possible error of one day if Shaban was seen, two days if not seen (due to possible error in Shaban itself).
5
Understand the extended case
The passage also considers if Rajab and Shaban were both counted without sighting; then the precaution is to fast 32 days if Shawwal is also obscured.
This shows the principle of erring on the side of caution.

Source Text

وفي البزازية وقعت في بخارى سنة إحدى وسبعين وسبعمائة أن الناس صاموا الأربعاء فجاء اثنان أو ثلاثة يوم الأربعاء التاسع والعشرين وأخبروا أنهم يوم رأوا ليلة الثلاثاء وهذا الأربعاء يوفي الثلاثين اتفقت الأجوبة أن بالسماء علة عيدوا يوم الخميس وإلا لا صاموا ثمانية وعشرين بلا رؤية ثم رأوا هلال الفطر إن أكملوا عدة شعبان ثلاثين وقد كانوا رأوا هلال شعبان قضوا يوماً، وإن صاموا تسعاً وعشرين لا قضاء عليهم أصلاً فإن كانوا أتموا شعبان من غير رؤية هلاله أيضاً قضوا يومين ا هـ . . كاملاً قوله : (فإن كانوا أتموا (شعبان) مقابل قوله وقد كانوا رأوا هلال شعبان» أي قضوا يوماً واحداً إن كانوا رأوا هلال شعبان، أما إن عدوه ثلاثين من غير رؤية أيضاً ثم صاموا رمضان ثمانية وعشرين قضوا يومين لأنه لم يعلم أن رمضان انتقص يوماً بيقين لجواز أنهم غلطوا في شعبان بيومين لما عدوه ثلاثين من غير رؤية كما في الولوالجية. وفي التتارخانية عن العتابية ولو رأوا هلال شعبان وعدوه ثلاثين يوماً ثم شرعوا في صوم رمضان فلما صاموا ثمانية وعشرين يوماً رأوا هلال شوال، فعليهم أن يقضوا يوماً واحداً لأنهم غلطوا بيوم واحد بيقين وإن عدوا شعبان ثلاثين يوماً من غير رؤية الهلال قضوا يومين لأنه يحتمل أنهم غلطوا من أول رمضان بيومين ا هـ . قلت : وبيانه أنهم إذا عدوا شعبان ثلاثين من غير رؤية هلال يحتمل أن يكونوا صاموا يومين من شعبان وأن رمضان وقع لأنه الأصل فعليهم قضاء يومين ثم الظاهر أن ما ذكر مفروض فيما إذا رؤي هلال رجب وعد ثلاثين ثم عد شعبان ثلاثين أيضاً لعدم رؤية هلالي شعبان ورمضان ثم رؤي هلال شوال بعد صوم ثمانية وعشرين، فلو غم هلال شوال أيضاً كيف يصنعون؟ لم أره والظاهر أنهم يصومون اثنين وثلاثين احتياطاً لاحتمال نقصان رجب وشعبان.
In al-Bazzaziyya, it occurred in Bukhara in the year 771 AH that the people fasted Wednesday, then two or three came on Wednesday, the twenty-ninth, and informed that they had seen [the crescent] on Tuesday night, and this Wednesday completed thirty. The answers agreed that if the sky had an obstruction, they should celebrate Eid on Thursday; otherwise, they would have fasted twenty-eight days without a sighting. Then they saw the crescent of Shawwal: if they completed the count of Shaban as thirty and they had seen the crescent of Shaban, they would make up one day; if they fasted twenty-nine, there is no makeup on them at all; if they completed Shaban without seeing its crescent, they would make up two days. [...] His statement: (if they completed Shaban) is an alternative to his statement 'and they had seen the crescent of Shaban,' meaning they would make up one day if they had seen the crescent of Shaban. As for if they counted it as thirty without a sighting also, then they fasted Ramadan twenty-eight days, they would make up two days because it is not known with certainty that Ramadan decreased by one day, due to the possibility that they erred in Shaban by two days when they counted it as thirty without sighting, as in al-Walwalijiyya. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Utabiyya: if they saw the crescent of Shaban and counted it as thirty days, then they started fasting Ramadan, then when they had fasted twenty-eight days they saw the crescent of Shawwal, they must make up one day because they erred by one day with certainty. And if they counted Shaban as thirty days without sighting the crescent, they make up two days because it is possible they erred from the beginning of Ramadan by two days. I say: its explanation is that if they counted Shaban as thirty without sighting the crescent, it is possible that they fasted two days of Shaban and that Ramadan occurred because it is the original, so they must make up two days. Then the apparent is that what is mentioned is assumed for the case when the crescent of Rajab was seen and counted as thirty, then Shaban was counted as thirty also due to not seeing the crescents of Shaban and Ramadan, then the crescent of Shawwal was seen after fasting twenty-eight days. If the crescent of Shawwal is also obscured, how should they act? I have not seen it, but apparently they should fast thirty-two as a precaution due to the possibility of Rajab and Shaban being deficient.
Source pages p. 467

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): making up missed fasts due to uncertainty
عدة (iddah): count of days (here referring to completing the count of Shaban)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Bukhara case, if the people had seen the crescent of Shaban and counted it as thirty days, then fasted Ramadan for 28 days and saw the crescent of Shawwal, how many days must they make up?
A) None
B) One day
C) Two days
D) Thirty days

Key Takeaway
The number of qada' days when Ramadan is uncertain depends on whether the start of Shaban was confirmed by sighting: one day if confirmed, two days if not.

Requirement of a Multitude for Crescent Sighting in Clear Sky
Establishes the Hanafi ruling for clear sky and refutes objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling requiring a great multitude for crescent sighting in a clear sky, and evaluate the evidence from qiyas against the opposing view.

Core Idea
When the sky is clear, the Hanafi school requires a multitude because a solitary report from a crowd is inherently suspect.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a key difference between the Hanafi school and its critics regarding the number of witnesses needed to confirm the crescent when the sky is clear. While the general rule in Islamic law is to accept two upright witnesses, the Hanafi school here requires a larger group (jama' 'azim) based on a powerful analogy (qiyas) from hadith transmission. The author defends this position against allegations of lacking evidence, and then offers a practical concession for later times.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
When the sky is clear, a great multitude (jama' 'azim) is required so that their report yields strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann).
This is the ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the opposing view
Critics claim that two witnesses should suffice, citing Allah's command to bring two witnesses. There is also a narration from Abu Hanifa (via Hasan) accepting two.
The opposing school (e.g., Shafi'i) does not require a multitude.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is a qiyas: just as a single narrator reporting an addition in a gathering is rejected because tafarrud (uniqueness) indicates error, similarly a single person seeing the crescent in a crowd is likely mistaken.
The qiyas is khafi (hidden) because the effective cause is tafarrud.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to critics
The author rebuts critics by asserting that qiyas is a valid proof in the absence of explicit text (sama'). The analogy is sound because its pillar (asl) and conditions are met.
The variation in eyesight does not weaken the analogy, as hearing also varies in the original ruling.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and later recommendation
In practice, requiring a multitude makes it difficult to establish the crescent. Therefore, later mashayikh recommend acting on the narration from Abu Hanifa (accepting two) due to people's negligence.
This is an example of taqyid (restriction) based on circumstance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإلا فجمع عظيم أي وإن لم يكن بالسماء علة فيهما يشترط أن يكون فيهما الشهود جمعاً كثيراً يقع العلم بخبرهم أي علم غالب الظن لا اليقين لأن التفرد من بين الجم الغفير بالرؤية مع توجههم طالبين لما توجه هو إليه مع فرض عدم المانع وسلامة الأبصار وإن تفاوتت الأبصار في الحدة ظاهر في غلطه قياساً على تفرد ناقل زيادة من بين سائر أهل مجلس مشاركين له في السماع فإنها ترد وإن كان ثقة مع أن التفاوت في حدة السمع واقع أيضاً كما في الإبصار مع أنه لا نسبة لمشاركته في السماع بمشاركته في الترائي كثرة، والزيادة المقبولة ما علم فيه تعدد المجالس أو جهل فيه الحال من الاتحاد والتعدد. كذا في فتح القدير وغيره. وبهذا اندفع تشنيع المتعصبين في زماننا على مذهبنا حيث زعموا أن عدم قبول الاثنين لا دليل له وهو مردود لأن القياس حيث لا سمع أحد الأدلة الشرعية والقياس المذكور صحيح لوجود ركنه وشرائطه ولم يريدوا بالتفرد تفرد الواحد وإلا لأفاد قبول الاثنين وهو منتف، بل المراد تفرد من لم يقع العلم بخبرهم من بين أضعافهم من الخلائق وهذا هو ظاهر الرواية. وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه يقبل فيه شهادة رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين، سواء كان بالسماء علة أو لم يكن كما روي عنه في هلال رمضان. كذا في البدائع. ولم أر من رجحها من المشايخ وينبغي العمل عليها في زماننا لأن الناس تكاسلت عن ترائي الأهلة فانتفى قولهم مع توجههم طالبين لما توجه هو إليه فكان التفرد غير ظاهر في الغلط، ولهذا وقع في زماننا في سنة خمس وخمسين وتسعمائة أن أهل مصر افترقوا فرقتين، فمنهم من صام ومنهم من لم يصم . وهكذا وقع لهم في الفطر بسبب أن جمعاً قليلاً شهدوا عند قاضي القضاة
His statement: (otherwise, a great multitude) means: if there is no obstruction in the sky in both [the beginning and end of Ramadan], then it is a condition that the witnesses be a large multitude such that knowledge occurs from their report, meaning knowledge of predominant probability, not certainty. Because the uniqueness of one person from among the great multitude in sighting, while they are all seeking what he seeks, assuming no obstacle and sound eyesight, even if eyesight varies in sharpness, is apparent in his error, by analogy to the uniqueness of one who reports an addition from among all the people of a gathering who share in hearing it: it is rejected even if he is trustworthy, even though the variation in sharpness of hearing also occurs as in eyesight, and there is no comparison between his participation in hearing and his participation in sighting in terms of abundance. The acceptable addition is when separation of assemblies is known or the situation of union or separation is unknown. This is in Fath al-Qadir and others. And by this, the criticism of the bigots in our time against our madhhab is repelled, where they claimed that the non-acceptance of two witnesses has no evidence, and it is refuted because analogy, where there is no transmitted text, is one of the legal evidences, and the mentioned analogy is sound due to its pillar and conditions. And they did not mean by 'uniqueness' the uniqueness of one, because that would imply acceptance of two, which is not the case. Rather, what is meant is the uniqueness of one whose report does not yield knowledge among the multitudes of people. And this is the apparent narration. And al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he accepts therein the testimony of two men or one man and two women, whether the sky has an obstruction or not, as narrated from him regarding the crescent of Ramadan. This is in al-Bada'i. And I have not seen any of the mashayikh who preferred it, but it is proper to act upon it in our time because people have become lazy in sighting the crescents, so their statement with them seeking what he seeks is nullified, and thus the uniqueness is not apparent in error. For this reason, it occurred in our time in the year 955 AH that the people of Egypt split into two groups: some fasted and some did not fast. And similarly, it occurred to them in breaking the fast because a small group testified before the chief qadi.
Source pages p. 468

Key Terms
جمع عظيم (jama' 'azim): a large multitude whose report creates strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann)
تفرد (tafarrud): uniqueness or solitary nature of a report among those equally capable
قياس (qiyas): analogical reasoning used as proof when no transmitted text exists

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the requirement for witnesses when the sky is clear for both Ramadan and Shawwal?
A) Two men or one man and two women
B) A large multitude whose report creates strong presumption
C) Any number of upright witnesses
D) Only one witness is sufficient

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi requirement of a multitude for clear-sky crescent sighting is based on a valid analogy (qiyas) from hadith transmission, but due to later negligence, acting on the lenient narration is recommended.

Ruling on Consecutive Complete or Deficient Months for Sighting
Explains the astronomical basis for assuming Shaban is deficient if prior months are full.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule regarding the assumption of Shaban's length based on the pattern of preceding months and apply it to determine the status of Shaban when sighting is obscured.

Core Idea
If four consecutive months before Shaban were full, Shaban must be considered deficient – an astronomical pattern supports this.

This lesson explores an auxiliary principle for determining the length of Shaban when the crescent is not sighted. Hanafi scholars, drawing from astronomical observations, have established that five consecutive full months do not occur, nor do four consecutive deficient months. This empirical rule helps maintain accurate lunar calendar calculations when direct sighting fails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition triggering the rule
Read the passage and determine the exact condition under which Shaban must be considered deficient. Look for the phrase 'إذا لم يتوال قبله أربعة على الكمال' (if four previous months have not been consecutive full months).
Condition: prior four months must all be full (30 days).
2
Apply the rule to the case
If the condition is met (four full months preceding Shaban), then Shaban is made deficient (29 days). Understand that this overrides the default assumption of completing Shaban to 30 days.
The rule is: 'جعل شعبان ناقصاً' (Shaban is made deficient).
3
Understand the rationale
The rule is based on astronomical consensus that five full months do not occur consecutively, nor do four deficient months. This provides a reliable pattern for when direct sighting is impossible.
Ahl al-miqat (astronomers) are the source of this knowledge.
4
Distinguish from primary proof
Note that this rule is not a substitute for crescent sighting. It is used only when sighting is obscure ('إن غم') and serves as supporting evidence, not a primary determinant.
The passage begins with 'وكذا ما قبله إن غم' (and similarly before it if obscure).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا ما قبله إن غم ولو شهوراً لا بحساب نجم وسير قمر على المشهور ، ثم نقل بعده قولاً آخر أنه يقيد قوله بكمال شعبان» بما إذا لم يتوال قبله أربعة على الكمال وإلا جعل شعبان ناقصاً لأنه لا يتوالى خمسة أشهر على الكمال كما لا يتوالى أربعة على النقص عند معظم أهل الميقات قال : ونظم (عج) كلامهم فقال : لا يتوالى النقص في أكثر من ثلاثة من الشهور يافطن كذا توالي خمسة مكملة هذا الصواب وما سواه أبـطـلـه ا هـ. قال: أي الصواب عند الميقاتيين وكذا قوله وما سواه
And similarly, what is before it, if it is obscure even for months, not by star calculation or moon's course, according to the well-known view. Then he transmitted another opinion after it that he restricts his statement 'by completing Shaban' to the case where not four previous months have been consecutive full months; otherwise, Shaban is made deficient because five months do not follow as full, just as four do not follow as deficient according to most astrologers. He said: and he (someone) versified their speech and said: 'Deficiency does not follow in more than three months, O attentive one. Likewise, the succession of five complete months is correct, and whatever is other than that is invalid.' He said: that is the correct view according to the astrologers, and so his statement and whatever is other than it.
Source pages p. 468

Key Terms
توالي (tawali): consecutiveness of months in being full (30 days) or deficient (29 days)
أهل الميقات (ahl al-miqat): astronomers or timekeepers who study lunar cycles

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if four consecutive months before Shaban have been full (30 days), what is the ruling regarding the sighting of Shawwal crescent?
A) Shaban is considered full (30 days) regardless
B) Shaban must be considered deficient (29 days)
C) The matter is left to witnesses
D) Astronomical calculation is used

Key Takeaway
When four consecutive months before Shaban are full, Shaban is considered deficient based on astronomical observation patterns.

The Hanafi Requirement of a Great Multitude for Crescent Sighting
Explains the Hanafi position on witness number for moon sighting in clear skies using qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of witnesses required for moon sighting in clear skies and explain the qiyas proof that supports it.

Core Idea
A single witness among a crowd is likely mistaken; thus a great multitude is required to produce legal certainty.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between clear and cloudy skies for moon sighting testimony. When the sky is clear, the possibility of error is high if only one or two witnesses claim to have seen the crescent while many others did not. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the requirement of a 'great multitude' and the analogy used to justify it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule from the matn
The matn states 'وإلا فجمع عظيم' meaning when the sky is clear, a great multitude is required. Understand that this applies when there is no atmospheric obstruction.
The matn is from Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
2
Understand the illa: solitariness indicating error
The sharh explains that a solitary witness among a crowd is likely mistaken, by analogy to a solitary narrator adding to a hadith that others did not hear. The effective cause (illa) is the solitariness despite the crowd seeking the same object.
This is a qiyas khafi (obscure analogy).
3
Examine the qiyas details
The analogy is drawn to the case of a reliable narrator who reports an addition that others present did not report; such an addition is rejected. Similarly, a single witness among a crowd that did not see the crescent is likely in error.
The qiyas is sound because the pillar and conditions of qiyas are present.
4
Distinguish from other madhahib
Unlike the Shafi'i school, which accepts two witnesses even in clear skies, the Hanafi school requires a great multitude due to this analogy. The text refutes critics who claim no proof for rejecting two witnesses.
The refutation is that the analogy is a valid legal proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإلا فجمع عظيم) أي وإن لم يكن بالسماء علة فيهما يشترط أن يكون فيهما الشهود جمعاً كثيراً يقع العلم بخبرهم أي علم غالب الظن لا اليقين لأن التفرد من بين الجم الغفير بالرؤية مع توجههم طالبين لما توجه هو إليه مع فرض عدم المانع وسلامة الأبصار وإن تفاوتت الأبصار في الحدة ظاهر في غلطه قياساً على تفرد ناقل زيادة من بين سائر أهل مجلس مشاركين له في السماع فإنها ترد وإن كان ثقة مع أن التفاوت في حدة السمع واقع أيضاً كما في الإبصار مع أنه لا نسبة لمشاركته في السماع بمشاركته في الترائي كثرة، والزيادة المقبولة ما علم فيه تعدد المجالس أو جهل فيه الحال من الاتحاد والتعدد. كذا في فتح القدير وغيره. وبهذا اندفع تشنيع المتعصبين في زماننا على مذهبنا حيث زعموا أن عدم قبول الاثنين لا دليل له وهو مردود لأن القياس حيث لا سمع أحد الأدلة الشرعية والقياس المذكور صحيح لوجود ركنه وشرائطه ولم يريدوا بالتفرد تفرد الواحد وإلا لأفاد قبول الاثنين وهو منتف، بل المراد تفرد من لم يقع العلم بخبرهم من بين أضعافهم من الخلائق وهذا هو ظاهر الرواية. وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه يقبل فيه شهادة رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين، سواء كان بالسماء علة أو لم يكن كما روي عنه في هلال رمضان. كذا في البدائع. ولم أر من رجحها من المشايخ وينبغي العمل عليها في زماننا لأن الناس تكاسلت عن ترائي الأهلة فانتفى قولهم مع توجههم طالبين لما توجه هو إليه فكان التفرد غير ظاهر في الغلط، ولهذا وقع في زماننا في سنة خمس وخمسين وتسعمائة أن أهل مصر افترقوا فرقتين، فمنهم من صام ومنهم من لم يصم . وهكذا وقع لهم في الفطر بسبب أن جمعاً قليلاً شهدوا عند قاضي القضاة الحنفي ولم يكن بالسماء علة فلم يقبلهم فصاموا وتبعهم جمع كثير على الصوم وأمروا الناس بالفطر، وهكذا في هلال الفطر حتى إن بعض المشايخ الشافعية صلى العيد بجماعة دون غالب أهل البلدة وأنكر عليه ذلك لمخالفة الإمام. ولم يقدر الجمع الكثير في ظاهر الرواية بشيء فروي عن أبي يوسف أنه قدره بعدد القسامة خمسين رجلاً، وعن محمد أنه يفوض مقدار القلة والكثرة إلى رأي الإمام. كذا في البدائع. وفي فتح القدير: والحق ما روي عن محمد وأبي يوسف أيضاً أن العبرة لتواتر الخبر ومجيئه من كل جانب. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية : وإن كانت السماء مصحبة لا تقبل شهادة الواحد في ظاهر الرواية بل يشترط العدد واختلفوا في تقديره ا هـ . فظاهره أن ظاهر الرواية لا يشترط الجمع العظيم وإنما يشترط العدد وهو يصدق على اثنين فكان مرجحاً لرواية الحسن التي اخترناها آنفاً، ويدل على ذلك أيضاً ما في الفتاوى الولوالجية : وإن كانت السماء مصحية لا تقبل شهادة الواحد، وعن أبي حنيفة أنه يقبل لأن اجتمع في هذه الشهادة ما يوجب القبول وهو العدالة والإسلام وما يوجب الرد وهو مخالفة الظاهر فرجح ما يوجب القبول احتياطاً لأنه إذا صام يوماً من شعبان كان خيراً من أن يفطر يوماً من رمضان. وجه ظاهر الرواية أنه اجتمع ما يوجب القبول وما يوجب الرد فرجح جانب الرد لأن الفطر في رمضان من كل وجه جائز يطمئن القلب إلا بالجمع العظيم فقد رأيت من الافتراء عليه ما لا يوصف فتعين العمل بظاهر المذهب لما فيه من اطمئنان الفؤاد ولما أنه لا يجوز العمل بخلافه وما عداه ليس بمذهب لنا كما نصوا عليه فاعلم ذلك. وقوله لأن الناس تكاسلت غير مسلم على الإطلاق بل المشاهد الاهتمام منهم والاجتهاد والنشاط إلى ذلك ولا عبرة بتكاسل البعض القليل تأمل . ا ... قلت: كأنه يتكلم على ما في زمانه وبلده وإلا فحال أهل زماننا لا يخفى على المشاهد ولو قدروا على الإفطار بالكلية لفعلوا وكثيراً ما نراهم يشتمون الشاهد ويغتابونه لسعيه في منعهم عن شهواتهم، وقد وقع في زماننا سنة خمس وعشرين بعد المائتين والألف أنهم أثبتوا رمضان بشهادة واحد على قول الطحاوي فحصل لذلك الشاهد من الناس غاية الإيذاء والإيجاع بالكلام حتى استفاض الخبر عن أكثر البلدان أنهم صاموا مثلنا، وشهد جماعة لدى القاضي على حكم قاضي ثغر بيروت فاكتف الناس عنه وبلغني أنه أقسم أن لا يشهد مرة ثانية وخصوصاً في بلدتنا دمشق فإنه قل ما يرى الهلال فيها في ليلته، وقد وقع في زمني غير مرة قضاؤنا يوماً أفطرناه من أوله فلا جرم أن عول الناس في زماننا على ما اختاره المؤلف. قوله : (وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية (الخ) ونحوه في الذخيرة حيث قال : لا تقبل شهادة الواحد في ظاهر الرواية خلافاً لما روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة، يحتاج فيه إلى زيادة العدد. واختلفوا في مقدار ذلك، روى الحسن بن زياد عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنه يقبل شهادة رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين، وعن أبي يوسف أنه يعتبر قدره بعد القسامة. ونحوه في التتارخانية فقال : لا تقبل شهادة الواحد في
His saying: (And otherwise a great multitude) meaning even if there is no atmospheric condition in them, it is required that the witnesses be a large group whose report produces certainty—meaning predominant conjecture, not certainty—because one's solitary sighting among a huge crowd, while they are all seeking what he is seeking, assuming no impediment and sound vision even if vision differs in sharpness, is evidently an error, by analogy to the solitary narrator reporting an addition among other attendees of a session who shared the hearing; such addition is rejected even if reliable, even though difference in hearing sharpness also occurs as in vision, though there is no comparison in terms of multiplicity between his participation in hearing and his participation in seeing. An accepted addition is one where multiple sessions are known or the situation (whether united or multiple) is unknown. Thus in Fath al-Qadir and others. By this, the criticism of fanatics in our time against our school is refuted, for they claim that the non-acceptance of two has no evidence, and it is rejected because analogy is one of the legal proofs where there is no transmitted evidence, and the mentioned analogy is sound because its pillar and conditions exist. They did not mean by 'solitariness' the solitariness of a single person, for then it would imply acceptance of two, which is negated; rather, they meant solitariness of one whose report does not produce certainty among the masses. This is the apparent narration. And al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he accepts in it the testimony of two men or one man and two women, whether there is an atmospheric condition or not, as narrated from him regarding the crescent of Ramadan. Thus in al-Bada'i. I have not seen any of the scholars preferring it, but one should act upon it in our time because people have become lazy about observing the crescents, so their being seekers is negated, and thus solitariness is not evidently erroneous. Hence in our time, in the year 955, the people of Egypt split into two groups: some fasted and some did not. Similarly, they had a dispute in breaking the fast because a small group testified before the chief qadi (Hanafi) when there was no atmospheric condition, and he did not accept them, so they fasted and a large group followed them, ordering people to break the fast. Similarly for the crescent of Eid, to the extent that some Shafi'i scholars prayed Eid with a congregation without most of the townspeople, and they were rebuked for opposing the imam. And the great multitude in the apparent narration was not defined by anything. It is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he defined it as the number of the qasama (fifty men). From Muhammad that he delegates the determination of smallness and largeness to the imam's opinion. Thus in al-Bada'i. In Fath al-Qadir: The truth is what is narrated from Muhammad and Abu Yusuf that the criterion is widespread report and coming from all sides. In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya: If the sky is clear, the testimony of one is not accepted in the apparent narration; rather, number is required, and they differed in its estimation. So its apparent meaning is that the apparent narration does not require the great multitude but only number, which applies to two, thus strengthening the narration of al-Hasan which we have chosen earlier. Also indicated by what is in al-Fatawa al-Walwalijiyya: If the sky is clear, the testimony of one is not accepted, and from Abu Hanifa that he accepts because in this testimony there is what necessitates acceptance—integrity and Islam—and what necessitates rejection—contradiction of the apparent—so the cause of acceptance is preponderated out of precaution because if he fasts a day of Sha'ban it is better than breaking a day of Ramadan. The basis of the apparent narration is that what necessitates acceptance and rejection exist together, so the side of rejection is preponderated because breaking Ramadan in every way is permissible; the heart is assured only by the great multitude. I have seen such defamation against him that cannot be described, so it is necessary to act upon the apparent madhhab for its reassurance of the heart, since acting contrary is not permissible and anything else is not our madhhab, as they have stated. So know that. And his statement 'because people have become lazy' is not accepted absolutely; rather, what is observed is their attention, effort, and activity, and the laziness of a few is not considered. Ponder... I said: He seems to speak of his own time and country; otherwise the condition of people in our time is not hidden from the observer. If they could break fast entirely they would, and often we see them insulting the witness and backbiting him for striving to prevent them from their desires. In our time, in the year 1225, they established Ramadan on the testimony of one based on al-Tahawi's opinion, and that witness suffered extreme harm and pain from people's speech until the news became well-known among most countries that they fasted like us. A group testified before the qadi based on the ruling of the qadi of the port of Beirut, and the people criticized him, and I was told that he swore not to testify again, especially in our town Damascus, for the crescent is rarely seen there on its night. Several times in my time we have had to make up a day that we broke from its beginning. Thus it is inevitable that people in our time rely on what the author chose. His saying: (In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya etc.) and similar in al-Dhakhira where it said: The testimony of one is not accepted in the apparent narration, contrary to what al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa; it requires increase in number. They differed in its amount. Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifa that he accepts the testimony of two men or one man and two women. From Abu Yusuf that he considers it to be the number of the qasama. And similar in al-Tatarkhaniyya: it said: The testimony of one is not accepted in...
Source pages p. 468

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, dealing with the requirement for witnesses testifying to the sighting of the crescent moon when the sky is clear (i.e., no atmospheric obstruction). The matn states: 'otherwise a great multitude' meaning that when there is no cloud or haze, a large number of witnesses is required. The sharh explains that 'great multitude' means such a number that their report produces certainty of the heart (predominant conjecture). The reasoning is that if one person claims to have seen the crescent while a large crowd seeking it did not see it, his claim is likely an error—by analogy to the case of a single narrator reporting an addition that others who were present did not hear. That addition is rejected even if the narrator is trustworthy. This analogy is used to argue that rejecting a single witness for moon sighting in clear skies is valid. The text then addresses critics who claim the Hanafi school has no evidence for rejecting two witnesses. It responds that the analogy is sound because there is no explicit textual evidence (sam') here, and the 'solitariness' meant is not that of a single person (which would accept two) but rather the solitariness of one whose report does not produce certainty among the masses. This is the position of the 'zahir al-riwaya' (the authoritative transmitted school position).

Key Terms
جمع عظيم (jam' 'azim): A large multitude whose testimony produces predominant conjecture (غالب الظن) that the crescent has been sighted.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The well-known transmitted position of the Hanafi school from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, as recorded in the six authoritative books.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given before a judge to establish a legal fact, here specifically sighting the crescent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the zahir al-riwaya of the Hanafi school, what is required for crescent sighting testimony when the sky is clear?
A) Two male witnesses
B) One male witness
C) A large multitude whose report produces predominant conjecture
D) Fifty witnesses exactly

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a great multitude for crescent sighting in clear skies, based on analogical reasoning from hadith transmission.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Moon Sighting Testimony
Details the intra-Hanafi dispute on witness number for moon sighting and the author's practical adaptation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the different opinions within the Hanafi school on the number of witnesses required for crescent sighting and evaluate the author's recommendation to act on the minority opinion due to changed circumstances.

Core Idea
Despite the madhhab's main position requiring a great multitude, later Hanafis considered adopting the minority view due to practical necessity.

Not all Hanafi imams agreed on the number of witnesses for crescent sighting. Some narrated from Abu Hanifa himself that two men or one man and two women suffice. Abu Yusuf required fifty, and Muhammad left it to the imam's discretion. This lesson explores the dispute and how a later Hanafi jurist, Ibn Nujaym, considered applying the minority view in his time due to people's negligence in moon watching.

Guided Path
1
State the main position (zahir al-riwaya) and its proof
The zahir al-riwaya requires a great multitude based on qiyas (solitary narrator analogy). This is the well-known school position.
See Lesson 1 for details.
2
Present the opposing narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa
Al-Hasan narrated that Abu Hanifa accepted the testimony of two men or one man and two women, regardless of sky condition, based on ihtiyat (precaution).
This narration is from nawadir (rare transmissions).
3
Note the variations: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Abu Yusuf required fifty witnesses (analogy to qasama). Muhammad left the number to the imam's discretion, making it flexible.
These show a spectrum of opinions.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference
If only two witnesses come in clear skies, according to the main view they are rejected; according to al-Hasan's narration they are accepted, and Ramadan begins.
The author gives historical examples (year 955 and 1225) where this caused community splits.
5
Consider the author's tarjih
Ibn Nujaym (author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) suggests acting on the minority view in his time because people became lazy in moon watching, so the illa (solitariness) no longer holds. He argues that the minority view was not preferred by earlier scholars but circumstances changed.
This is a pragmatic application of usul al-iftah considering changing customs.

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, dealing with the requirement for witnesses testifying to the sighting of the crescent moon when the sky is clear (i.e., no atmospheric obstruction). The matn states: 'otherwise a great multitude' meaning that when there is no cloud or haze, a large number of witnesses is required. The sharh explains that 'great multitude' means such a number that their report produces certainty of the heart (predominant conjecture). The reasoning is that if one person claims to have seen the crescent while a large crowd seeking it did not see it, his claim is likely an error—by analogy to the case of a single narrator reporting an addition that others who were present did not hear. That addition is rejected even if the narrator is trustworthy. This analogy is used to argue that rejecting a single witness for moon sighting in clear skies is valid. The text then addresses critics who claim the Hanafi school has no evidence for rejecting two witnesses. It responds that the analogy is sound because there is no explicit textual evidence (sam') here, and the 'solitariness' meant is not that of a single person (which would accept two) but rather the solitariness of one whose report does not produce certainty among the masses. This is the position of the 'zahir al-riwaya' (the authoritative transmitted school position).

Key Terms
جمع عظيم (jam' 'azim): A large multitude whose testimony produces predominant conjecture (غالب الظن) that the crescent has been sighted.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The well-known transmitted position of the Hanafi school from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, as recorded in the six authoritative books.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given before a judge to establish a legal fact, here specifically sighting the crescent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which Hanafi scholar required fifty witnesses for crescent sighting, according to the passage?
A) Abu Hanifa in the narration of al-Hasan
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) Ibn Nujaym

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has internal disagreement on witness number for moon sighting, with the operative position (zahir al-riwaya) requiring a great multitude, but later jurists considered the minority view in response to social change.

Sawm — Fasting

Witness Requirements for Moon Sighting: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Number when Sky is Clear
Explains Hanafi dispute on number of witnesses for moon sighting in clear skies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the main Hanafi positions regarding the number of witnesses required for moon sighting when the sky is clear and explain the tarjih (preponderance) of the zahir al-riwayah over the single-witness narration.

Core Idea
When the sky is clear, testimony of a single just witness is not accepted in the Hanafi zahir al-riwayah; multiple witnesses are required to eliminate doubt.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: how many witnesses are needed to confirm the sighting of the new moon for Ramadan when the sky is clear? While some narrations from Abu Hanifa accept a single witness, the established transmitted position (zahir al-riwayah) requires a larger number. Understanding this dispute clarifies the evidentiary standards for starting and ending Ramadan and highlights how Hanafi jurists balance precaution against the apparent state of the sky. The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the arguments and the author's preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine whether the sky is clear (mus-hiyah) or cloudy. The ruling differs based on this condition.
Clear sky means no cloud or dust that would normally obscure the crescent.
2
State the Zahir al-Riwayah position
According to the established transmitted narration, a single witness is not accepted when the sky is clear; a number of witnesses is required.
The exact number is not specified in zahir al-riwayah, but it is more than one.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify the different opinions: a) Narration by al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa accepts a single witness (or two men or one man and two women). b) Abu Yusuf requires a large group (fifty by qasamah). c) Muhammad leaves it to the judge’s discretion. d) Others specify 500 or two from each mosque.
These are all transmitted within the Hanafi school, but only one is considered the madhhab.
4
Analyze the tarjih criteria
The author prefers the zahir al-riwayah over the single-witness narration because the heart is not assured without a large group, and opposing the apparent (clear sky) requires caution. He considers the single-witness narration as shadhdh (odd).
The principle: when acceptance and rejection factors conflict, rejection prevails because fasting is not obligatory based on doubt.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
If a single trustworthy person reports sighting the moon when the sky is clear, the judge should not accept it. He should wait for multiple witnesses. If the witness comes from outside the city or from a high place, the testimony is accepted even if single.
This exception is based on higher certainty due to lack of dust and obstacles.

كتاب الصوم
الحنفي ولم يكن بالسماء علة فلم يقبلهم فصاموا وتبعهم جمع كثير على الصوم وأمروا الناس بالفطر، وهكذا في هلال الفطر حتى إن بعض المشايخ الشافعية صلى العيد بجماعة دون غالب أهل البلدة وأنكر عليه ذلك لمخالفة
