مخالفة الظاهر فرجح ما يوجب القبول احتياطاً لأنه إذا صام يوماً من شعبان كان خيراً من أن يفطر يوماً من رمضان وجه ظاهر الرواية أنه اجتمع ما يوجب القبول وما يوجب الرد فرجح جانب الرد لأن الفطر في رمضان من كل وجه جائز يطمئن القلب إلا بالجمع العظيم فقد رأيت من الافتراء عليه ما لا يوصف فتعين العمل بظاهر المذهب لما فيه ومن اطمئنان الفؤاد ولما أنه لا يجوز العمل بخلافه وما عداه ليس بمذهب لنا كما نصوا عليه فاعلم ذلك. وقوله لأن الناس تكاسلت غير مسلم على الإطلاق بل المشاهد الاهتمام منهم والاجتهاد والنشاط إلى ذلك ولا عبرة بتكاسل البعض القليل تأمل . ا ... قلت: كأنه يتكلم على ما في زمانه وبلده وإلا فحال أهل زماننا لا يخفى على المشاهد ولو قدروا على الإفطار بالكلية لفعلوا وكثيراً ما نراهم يشتمون الشاهد ويغتابونه لسعيه في منعهم عن شهواتهم، وقد وقع في زماننا سنة خمس وعشرين بعد المائتين والألف أنهم أثبتوا رمضان بشهادة واحد على قول الطحاوي فحصل لذلك الشاهد من الناس غاية الإيذاء والإيجاع بالكلام حتى استفاض الخبر عن أكثر البلدان أنهم صاموا مثلنا، وشهد جماعة لدى القاضي على حكم قاضي ثغر بيروت فاكتف الناس عنه وبلغني أنه أقسم أن لا يشهد مرة ثانية وخصوصاً في بلدتنا دمشق فإنه قل ما يرى الهلال فيها في ليلته، وقد وقع في زمني غير مرة قضاؤنا يوماً أفطرناه من أوله فلا جرم أ أن عول الناس في زماننا على ما اختاره المؤلف قوله : (وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية (الخ) ونحوه في الذخيرة حيث قال : لا تقبل شهادة الواحد في ظاهر الرواية خلافاً لما روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة، يحتاج فيه إلى زيادة العدد. واختلفوا في مقدار ذلك، روى الحسن بن زياد عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنه يقبل شهادة رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين، وعن أبي يعتبر قدره بعد القاسمة الخ. ونحوه في التتارخانية فقال : لا تقبل شهادة الواحد في يوسف أنه حر وحرتين للفطر وإلا فجمع عظيم والأضحى كالفطر ولا عبرة باختلاف المطالع .
ذلك بعذر كما في المريض والمسافر، وصوم رمضان قبل رمضان لا يجوز بعذر من الأعذار فكان المصير إلى ما يجوز بعذر أولى . ثم إذا لم تقبل شهادة الواحد واحتيج إلى زيادة العدد عن أبي حنيفة أنه تقبل شهادة رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين، وعن أبي يوسف أنه لا يقبل ما لم يشهد على جمع عظيم وذلك مقدر بعدد القسامة، وعن خلف بن أيوب خمسمائة ببلخ قليل، وعن أبي حفص الكبير أنه شرط الوفا، وعن محمد ما استكثره الحاكم فهو كثير وما استقله فهو قليل. هذا إذا كان الذي شهد بذلك في المصر، أما إذا جاء من مكان آخر خارج المصر فإنه تقبل شهادته إذا كان عدلاً ثقة لأنه يتيقن في الرؤية في الصحاري ما لم يتيقن في الأمصار لما فيها من كثرة الغبار، وكذا إذا كان في المصر في موضع مرتفع وهلال الفطر إذا كانت السماء مصحية كهلال رمضان ا هـ. فهذا يدل على ترجيح رواية الحسن وأن ظاهر الرواية اعتبار العدد لا الجمع الكثير لكن فرقه بين من كان بالمصر وخارجه وبين المكان المرتفع وغيره قول الطحاوي : : أما ظاهر الرواية فلا يقبل فيه خبر الواحد مطلقاً كما في غاية البيان وفتح القدير قوله : (والأضحى (كالفطر) أي هلال ذي الحجة كهلال شوال فلا يثبت بالغيم إلا برجلين أو رجل وامرأتين، وأما حالة الصحو فالكل سواء لا بد من زيادة العدد على ما قدمناه، وإنما كان كهلاله دون رمضان لأنه تعلق به حق العباد وهو التوسع بلحوم الأضاحي. وذكر في النوادر عن أبي حنيفة أنه كرمضان لأنه تعلق به أمر ديني وهو وجوب الأضحية، والأول ظاهر المذهب كذا في الخلاصة. وهو ظاهر الرواية وهو الأصح كذا في الهداية وشروحها والتبيين. وصحح الثاني صاحب التحفة فاختلف التصحيح لكن تأيد الأول بأنه المذهب ولم يتعرض لحكم بقية الأهلة التسعة. وذكر الإمام الأسبيجابي في شرح مختصر الطحاوي الكبير : وأما في هلال الفطر والأضحى وغيرهما من الأهلة فإنه لا يقبل فه إلا شهادة رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين عدول أحرار غير محدودين كما في سائر الأحكام اهـ.
ظاهر الرواية خلافاً لما روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة بل يحتاج فيه إلى زيادة العدد واختلفوا في مقدار ذلك الخ. وفيها عن الحجة ولو قبل الإمام شهادة شاهدين عدلين وقد سقط قلب القاضي على قولهما جاز وثبت حكم رمضان .
قوله : (قول الطحاوي) خبر قوله «فرق». وفي الذخيرة : إنما لا تقبل شهادة الواحد على هلال رمضان إذا كانت السماء مصحية إذا كان هذا الواحد في المصر، وأما إذا جاء خارج المصر أو جاء من أعلى الأماكن في مصر ذكر الطحاوي رحمه الله أنه تقبل شهادته، وهكذا ذكر في كتاب الاستحسان. وذكر في القدوري أنه لا تقبل شهادته في ظاهر الرواية، وذكر الكرخي أنه تقبل، وفي الأقضية : صحح رواية الطحاوي واعتمد عليها قوله : (فإنه لا يقبل فيه إلا شهادة رجلين الخ) قال الرملي : الظاهر أنه في الأهلة التسعة لا فرق بين يكون في السماء علة أم لا في قبول الرجلين أو
Book of Fasting. The Hanafi—and there was no cloud in the sky—so he did not accept them, and they fasted and a large group followed them in fasting and they ordered the people to break the fast. Similarly for the crescent of Fitr, such that some Shafi'i scholars prayed Eid with a congregation without the majority of the city’s people and were criticized for opposing the Imam. And the large group is not quantified in zahir al-riwayah. It is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he quantified it as the number of qasama, fifty men. From Khalaf ibn Ayyub: five hundred in Balkh is few. Some said: it should be one or two congregations from each mosque. From Muhammad: he delegates the amount of fewness and manyness to the Imam’s opinion. Thus in al-Bada'i. In Fath al-Qadir: the truth is what is narrated from Muhammad and Abu Yusuf also: the criterion is the widespread report and its coming from every side. In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya: if the sky is clear, the testimony of one is not accepted in zahir al-riwayah, rather number is required and they differed in its quantification. End. Zahir al-riwayah does not require a large group but only number, which applies to two, so it supports the narration of al-Hasan which we chose earlier. Also indicated by what is in al-Fatawa al-Walwalijiyya: if the sky is clear, the testimony of one is not accepted. From Abu Hanifa: it is accepted because in this testimony there are factors that require acceptance (justice and Islam) and factors that require rejection (opposing the apparent), so the factor requiring acceptance is given preponderance as a precaution because fasting a day of Sha'ban is better than breaking a day of Ramadan. The argument of zahir al-riwayah: factors requiring acceptance and rejection are present, so the rejection side is given preponderance because breaking fast in Ramadan is permissible in every way. The heart is not reassured except with a large group. I have seen slanders against him beyond description. So it is necessary to act on the apparent madhhab for that reason and for reassurance of the heart, and because acting contrary to it is not permissible, and anything else is not our madhhab as they stated. Know that. And his saying “because people have become lazy” is not accepted absolutely; rather what is witnessed is their concern, effort, and activity towards that, and no regard is given to the laziness of a few. Reflect. I said: it seems he speaks regarding his own time and city, otherwise the state of our time’s people is not hidden from the observer. If they could break fast entirely they would, and often we see them insulting the witness and backbiting him for his effort to prevent them from their desires. In our time, the year 1225, they confirmed Ramadan by the testimony of one on the opinion of al-Tahawi, and that witness received extreme harm and hurt through speech from the people, until the news spread from most cities that they fasted like us. A group testified before the judge on the ruling of the judge of the port of Beirut, and people were satisfied with it, and he told me he swore not to testify again, especially in our city Damascus, for rarely is the crescent seen there on its night. It has occurred in my time more than once that we spent a day breaking fast from its beginning. So it is no wonder that people in our time relied on what the author chose. His statement: (In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya) and similar in al-Dhakhira: the testimony of one is not accepted in zahir al-riwayah contrary to what al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa; it needs an increase in number. They differed in its amount. Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifa that the testimony of two men or one man and two women is accepted. From Abu Yusuf: it is not accepted until a large group testifies, quantified as the number of qasama. From Khalaf ibn Ayyub: five hundred in Balkh is few. From Abu Hafs al-Kabir: he set the condition of completion? From Muhammad: what the ruler deems many is many, and what he deems few is few. This is when the witness is in the city. If he comes from another place outside the city, his testimony is accepted if he is just and trustworthy, because he is certain of seeing in deserts compared to cities due to the abundance of dust. Similarly if he is in a high place in the city. And the crescent of Fitr when the sky is clear is like the crescent of Ramadan. End. This indicates the preponderance of the narration of al-Hasan, and that zahir al-riwaya considers number not the large group, but he distinguished between one in the city and outside, and between a high place and others. Al-Tahawi said: zahir al-riwaya does not accept the report of one absolutely, as in Ghayat al-Bayan and Fath al-Qadir. His statement: (and al-Adha is like al-Fitr) meaning the crescent of Dhul Hijjah is like the crescent of Shawwal, so it is not proven in cloudy [weather] except by two men or one man and two women. As for the clear state, all are the same; an increase in number is necessary as we have mentioned. It is like the crescent of Shawwal and not Ramadan because it involves a right of the servants, namely widening through the meat of sacrifices. In al-Nawadir from Abu Hanifa: it is like Ramadan because it involves a religious matter, the obligation of sacrifice. The first is the apparent madhhab as in al-Khulasa. It is zahir al-riwaya and the most correct as in al-Hidaya and its commentaries and al-Tabyin. The second was deemed correct by the author of al-Tuhfa, so correction differed, but the first is supported because it is the madhhab. He did not address the ruling of the remaining nine crescents. Imam al-Asbijabi in his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Tahawi al-Kabir said: regarding the crescent of Fitr and Adha and other crescents, only the testimony of two men or one man and two women, just and free and not flogged, is accepted, as in other legal matters. End. Zahir al-riwaya contrary to what al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa, rather it needs an increase in number, and they differed in its amount. And in it from al-Hujja: if the Imam accepted the testimony of two just witnesses and the judge's heart inclined to their statement, it is permissible and the ruling of Ramadan is established. His statement (saying of al-Tahawi) is the predicate of his word “he distinguished”. In al-Dhakhira: the testimony of one is not accepted for the crescent of Ramadan when the sky is clear, if that one is in the city. But if he comes from outside the city or from a high place in the city, al-Tahawi said: his testimony is accepted. Thus mentioned in Kitab al-Istihsan. In al-Quduri: his testimony is not accepted in zahir al-riwaya. Al-Karkhi said: it is accepted. In al-Aqdiya: he corrected the narration of al-Tahawi and relied on it. His statement: (only the testimony of two men etc.) al-Ramli said: apparently regarding the nine crescents there is no difference between whether there is a cloud in the sky or not in accepting two men or...
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of witnesses required for the sighting of the new moon of Ramadan and Shawwal. The author, Ibn Nujaym, begins by recounting a situation where the sky was clear and a single witness's testimony was accepted, leading to confusion. He then quotes various Hanafi authorities. The core issue: when the sky is clear (mus-hiyah), does the testimony of a single just witness suffice, or does it require multiple witnesses? Abu Hanifa, in a narration by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, accepts a single witness (or two men or one man and two women) as a precaution to avoid missing a day of Ramadan. However, the zahir al-riwayah (the established transmitted position) requires a number of witnesses, rejecting the single witness because breaking fast is generally permissible and the heart is not reassured without a large group. The author leans towards the zahir al-riwayah, emphasizing that the apparent madhhab must be followed. He then presents various opinions: Abu Yusuf requires a large group (like 50 as in qasama), Muhammad leaves it to the judge's discretion, and others suggest specific numbers. The passage also distinguishes between witnesses inside the city (where testimony is not accepted due to dust and uncertainty) and those coming from outside the city or from a high place (where it is accepted because of certainty). For Shawwal, the ruling is similar to Ramadan. The discussion then turns to the crescent of Dhul Hijjah for Eid al-Adha: the author states it is like Shawwal (requires two men or one man and two women), but al-Hasan narrates from Abu Hanifa that it is like Ramadan (requires the same as Ramadan). The first opinion is the apparent madhhab and the most correct. The passage ends by noting that other crescents require similar conditions, and al-Ramli opines that for all nine crescents, the requirement is two men or one man and two women regardless of sky condition. The author also relates a historical incident from 1225 AH where a single witness caused turmoil, leading many to rely on the author's chosen position. This commentary is a typical expansion probe, citing multiple sources and discussing the tarjih (preponderance) of opinions.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The established transmitted rulings from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad in the six core books of Muhammad al-Shaybani.
السماء مصحية (al-sama' mushiyah): A clear sky without clouds that would normally obscure the crescent.
القسامة (al-qasamah): A specific number (50) used in oaths for homicide cases; here used as a benchmark for a large group of witnesses.
جمع عظيم (jam'un 'azim): A large multitude of witnesses whose testimony brings certainty; quantified as 50 or more by some scholars.
هلال الفطر والأضحى (hilal al-fitr wa al-adha): The new moons of Shawwal (Eid al-Fitr) and Dhul Hijjah (Eid al-Adha). The passage debates whether they require the same evidence as Ramadan or a lesser standard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the zahir al-riwayah, what is the ruling on accepting a single witness's testimony for the moon sighting of Ramadan when the sky is clear?
A) It is accepted because the witness is just.
B) It is not accepted; a number of witnesses is required.
C) It is accepted only if the witness is a man.
D) It is accepted only if the witness is from outside the city.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when the sky is clear, the testimony of a single witness is insufficient to establish the crescent for Ramadan; multiple witnesses must testify to ensure certainty, following the zahir al-riwayah.
